There are several ways to perform the cautery, linking according to the length of the mouse (arrow), as described before for the liver cautery; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, let the patient lie on his back; another way of cauterizing is heating the cautery with two wires, as we showed in the shoulder dislocation; lift the skin where the mouse enters, or the boil comes towards the left side, and lift the incisions from the skin according to the skin, according to the length of the body, and let the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After placing the two inflamed nerves, heat them so that the holes are pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery; in this way there will be four holes, and if you see, cauterize at all three openings with the cautery.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After healing when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is worth doing what the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of the hydropieric disease
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Cauterization does not work against dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you treat it according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must make four cauterizations around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back near the spine, and at the worst spot; and let the cauteries be close to the affected area.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the fire cautery open to purge for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the abdomen is the clavicle as we have shown before; and that for the back is olive-shaped, as it is described above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in those who are dropsical and full of watery citrine, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and dip your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not go in too deep, as this would be too harsh on the watery citrine; and let the cautery be shaped like this:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit. de la menoison	of the emaciation

de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the hernia called "thelul"

When you apply the cautery to althelul, heat up the cautery that seems like a razor, and then place it all over the althelul to be cauterized; leave your hand there so that the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, so as not to miss it. de plaie mal curee	from an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear incision or opening, as we will explain in its place, this disease comes which cannot be cured except by cautery.

de la vessie	of the bladder

de la marris	of the marriage
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	of the haunch

de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the haunch
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the loin of the haunch, and it is due to coldness and moisture; the patient is treated as we have said in the division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterward, perform cautery; and the method of cautery is according to two methods: namely, with burning substances and fire cautery.

Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, perform the fire cautery on the circular cauterizer mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the thigh; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire thigh, and all the flesh around the wound is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the method that one does in sciatica, when pain persists in the hip, and cannot reach the thigh nor the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 If it comes to the thigh and the leg, one should perform a fire cautery at the place where pain persists, and the fire cautery should be four fingers deep at the left side of the ankle; and the cautery may be sharp, and the fat should be burned off; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two feet or close to it, the cauterization should be performed there where they feel pain three inches or four around the cauterization called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	If necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, perform a cautery with a scalpel-type or circular cauterizer, and be careful in all your cauterizations that you do not burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 Galen tells us of a cure in which a nobleman was cured from the pain of hemorrhoids and sciatica, and he praised it greatly, saying that there was no other cure, and that it became healed at once when this cure was made, and he bathed himself as indicated below.

And he said in this way that you take fresh and dry verditer powder and grind it very well with a little fat, and place it on the hemorrhoids and on the thigh and leg where the pain is, and hold it; and leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning.

Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take linen and anoint it with old oil, and place it over the furrow that is between the toe of the foot and the one called 'foscile'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 After taking dry sheep's fat and heat it until it becomes charcoal, place it on the linen, let it remain for a while, repeat this procedure again, and continue doing so as long as you think that it will reach the heel and that the pain will cease; this method of cautery is called 'sheep's fat cautery'.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When back pain comes from falling, or blows, or excessive bleeding, or similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these cases are worth using cauterization except for the one that comes from the infusion of cold matter.

Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees. de la dolor des jointes	For the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is due to moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured with cauteries in this manner: make a large amount of cautionery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautionery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if necessary, prick on the face of the foot, and make a cautery all over with a sharp point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make a cautery on each knee 3 or 4 times over all parts, with an olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand too far away from the heated iron.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend down to the knees and back, administer the fire cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 If the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist joints; and if no pain remains at the elbows, make incisions on each joint and along the wrist of the hand; and if the pains come down to the arms or shoulders, cauterize each part and administer good care to the patient and consider medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you provide good care and purge the phlegm, it will be healed with God's aid.
de la routure dou syfac	of the dislocation of the thigh
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When ruptures come in anger, and the intestines descend into the abdomen and it is newly formed, if you wish to cure it, it should not be touched that day; and it should be treated with things that relax the stomach, so that the intestines descend from the stomach. After doing this, make the patient sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm straight until the rupture is repaired, and bend them at your elbows, and press firmly on the site of the rupture above the wrist bone, and at a sign that resembles half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and yields pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then pull the bowels back to their place; and have the minister hold his hand so they do not return; work the thighs of the patient well, and put the cussin and serjant on the thighs, and another one on the affected area where he holds the hands; then place the cautery on the sign all over your hand, hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; be careful that the bowel does not come out while you are performing the cautery; do not burn it; and beware that the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 The cauterization of children should be subtle according to their size, and that of adults according to theirs; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; after that cure it with other remedies until it is healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well; and it is necessary that his urine be restrained for a long time, so that the scabs do not protrude when he gets up to go to the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, a cloth should be provided for him and kept on for forty other days; let him rest well, so that he does not overwork or eat too much and drink too much and speak too loudly; and when he follows these instructions, he will be completely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say afterwards the treatment of amputation in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the wound from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When roundworms come in other wombs and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, then make the cautery of the cautery according to its size, and let it be burned the third part of the belly; afterwards cure as we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a four-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first sign the position of the wound and make a line above the roundworm, and another below, and take your hand at the entire four-angled cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cauteries are lighter and more movable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or wounding, and that pain lasts a long time, and the medicine cures do not help, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twisting and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If the first cautery heals, that is good; but if not, you should start another cautery on it, because this custom is that it should change in the member which is close to it, so you should perform cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The illnesses are sometimes alleviated by cautery with great help, and the same applies to those that come from the corruption of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see the patient being cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, without sores or persistence, then you doubt that the corruption will affect the whole patient, then apply V cauteries on the head: First, turn the head towards you, and the other one towards the front to the end of the hairs; then on both temples, and behind the ears; and let your hand stay so that the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scorches come out as long as the vapors of large humors can escape; then cauterize the area where there is tumor according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is scattered everywhere, it manifests clearly that you must cauterize it with the cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery in the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttock and one other near it, and two on the hips; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are above the last ribs, lest you burn them; and sometimes do a cautery on the bone of the fist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more you perform cautery, the more help it provides, and it benefits them; and know that sick people feel no pain during cautery as healthy ones do, because their bodies are already all corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in ways of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After curing the wound with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it is drained.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When a swelling appears in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but is not healed, then do cautery on the member according to its size and smallness of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep into the flesh; then heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes a cautery is performed on the hand, foot and back, at the opening of the nerve that renders the limb motionless, and thus if the skin is removed; but no one should interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the openings of moving nerves.
de albaras	From the sling (or bandage)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness called "albaras" appears, and medical instruments are of no use, then cauterize it with a small hot iron, according to the thickness of the wound skin, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then treat it with flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, as well as the blood of a pig and the blood of an almond, each in turn; mix everything together, tie it up with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a boil begins to appear and you want to stop it, if you cauterize it with the cautery that seems circular all around the boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And the wise say that a cautery should be applied in the middle of the boil; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear it will ulcerate and decay, and I have seen it happen once; and a more appropriate thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular", as we said earlier concerning cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the inflammation that cannot grow larger
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to heal or because of the superfluity it makes or due to the age of the patient when they are very old and have little blood, or because of the time; if you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it in this state.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 It will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through and through with the fire-cautery, then heat the fire-cautery as described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and make sure the cauteries are such that the patient feels it outside in this way that the course of the pus is made easier.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the cure when he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another type of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but an erosion of a limb, because it consumes the limbs as fire dries out wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries, small and large, according to where the disease is located; after cauterizing all parts until you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, everything corrupted should be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and put on the affected areas soothing balm made with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the ointment treatment for generating heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if you see after three days that healthy heat does not arise, it is good; and if it does not, then perform the fire cautery again on the corrupted lesion.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this remedy has sometimes been cured with hot medicine instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for hot medicine in the section on disease: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The hairs which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Often it happens that in the foot there arises a disease called "clog" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing filled with pus that inflames the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, fire cautery and water hot cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Cautere of fire is when you heat the iron [or metal] like a feather on a hot coal, and it should be made of good iron to the size that can pierce through the nail from all sides, and have fine margins; then place everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it starts to melt; and leave it so for three days until it begins to emit pus; then make a plaster of bad herbs boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nails will shrink and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the joint with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if it is turned outward by the body and often happens in hands and feet, you should bring hot cautery; and this is done in such a way: take a rod of iron or copper, or a plumbers' pipe, and place it on top and the coal, which means to burn warts; and place the rod so that it surrounds completely, then put a little hot coal there, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the margin of the rod comes to the root of the coal, and can find the hot coal channeled down to the root; and let the patient endure a little bit of the bite of the hot coal for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will uproot itself completely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 As another follows, while you are heating all those who are within the body, then you care for the ointments that heal burns.
li cure dou trembler	The Cure for Trembling (literally: "the trembling care")
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	For some who tremble from coldness of the nerves or from quarter fever or any other illness, you should perform four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and one at the navel, and one above the stomach with the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling, and the healthiness will hasten away from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Putrid boils (literally: "smelly pustules")
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes, through the body, baths appear or pusulous wounds come from large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 At first, when they appear, it is necessary to perform a cauterization on each chief of the pus: a fine cautery made from mirte stick, from which the tip should be impregnated with fire, or from the long root of aristologue, or to the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes cauterization is done at the beginning when they appear in this way, and they cannot grow further, but the excess from which they come is broken up, and they are healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	At times, there are great discharges of blood from the cut artery that comes at an open wound or abscess incision, or to a cauterized limb, and similar things; it is a very serious matter to allow this to flow out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And furthermore, whenever this happens, hasten to place your finger on the vein wound, and hold it very tightly until the blood is stopped from flowing; then take olive oil cauteries, both small and large, until they are all red; then take one, either large or small depending on the wound and where the artery is located; and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped flowing.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If the vein jumps when you hold your finger on it and the cautery stops, take hastily another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to do this one after another until the blood is stopped flowing; and beware not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when the artery does not stop bleeding, it cannot be well stopped when the artery is large, unless this is done by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be tied and held in place accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies tight bandages or places hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit from it unless otherwise.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens and there is no medicine or remedy present, then put your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it tightly over the wound and the vein; do not move it but wet it with cold water often until the wound is very cold, frozen, swollen, and held in place; and follow the instructions for cauteries and medicines that are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which fire cautery or a burning medicine is required, and about their kinds, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter up to the feet, and I will go into this chapter through the same way because it will be easier for you to find those things that you are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I advise you not to attempt folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many ways of people come in treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 If people come who are healing themselves with their disease such that they die easily because of the insanity that arises from their illness and the greatness of its wickedness, then one must be afraid of them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And among these there are those who give you their sense and say "wait, I am cured"; but the disease is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 You should not easily consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but place more importance on your honor than on your desire, and do not give way thoughtlessly but wisely from those about whom you are certain, and from which you can take lessons; and use prediction and indication in the treatments of your patients so that health may be achieved; and this will help you acquire good renown, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, Our Lord grants you good understanding and righteousness, and if you desire to inspire by the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have organized this chapter in sections, as it is set out according to the chapter of cauteries, which I have previously explained from head to foot because you will find it easier to understand what is necessary.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full head swollen with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and sometimes it happens for reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all that I have seen hasten to death; therefore it seems to me worthwhile to abandon the work in some treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose neck was filled with water and his head swelled every day until he could no longer bear it; the moisture gathered under the skull bone between the skull and the bone; and since the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make an incision large in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can pass; and here is the form of a lancet:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscesses are larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone and you see the joints at the head of each part opening wide when pressed with your hand from within, and it does not respond to you: you must make three incisions in the head of the joint like this:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after incising, remove all moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 After making the incision, remove linens and powders, then apply wine and oil, let it be so until the fifth day; then unbind it, cure the wound with bandages and ointments, allow the head to swell, and give the patient dried meat of a moist animal until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe the size of the abscess and its source, for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, open where the abscess is located and drain the pus, and do as you are able; and be careful not to cover the artery; and let some blood flow, so that the patient may die a natural death due to bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Then take remedies made from rue herb.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When any disease called "catarrh" occurs among the eyes or in a worse condition and the medicine does not help at all, then the last remedy is the cautery with which two arteries will be covered.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you wish to cover it, the patient should lie with his head backwards; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then grasp the patient's neck with a cloth; then look where the veins are, and the ears are on either side, and the temples are behind; then mark the veins with ink; then strike one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts, until the cutting reaches the bone, but only along the width of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you wish, push the spatula under the artery and strike it from above, cutting as deep as two fingers through it.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is pricked, it should jump up without stopping repeatedly moving upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not open up on its own, you must measure the space of three feet, then make an incision to the bone; and that which needs blood to be removed is 6 cubic inches, and about a spoonful more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone without swelling, if the pus that comes from an abscess does not come out, then hold and bind the wound and treat it with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	from emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old emigration and acute catarrh come, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and ancient dementia and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medicine but none of it helps; if we open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extraction [of what is stuck] is that the patient tilts his head back towards the hairs on his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and can be easily located except in some very cold people; and if it has been located, the patient tightens his neck with some cloth, then rubs the area with a rough fabric, and scratches the area with warm water until the artery becomes manifestly apparent; then take the spatula as shown here:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then, gently scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up towards the prongs (clamps), and carefully remove the bands from both sides; if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the scissors, then squeeze that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 If it is not cut (or opened), it cannot move at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw the blood from the 5 cm to the 4th one; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with a thick silk thread, which prevents pus from coming before the wound of the incision, and allows the flow of blood; then cut off the excess between the two threads in that hour itself, and if you see, cauterize it with the cautery knife up to the bone until the shoulders are severed; and this is the mutilating work, if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are aid for curing the moisture; because it is of greater help to the moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place well-made tourniquets on it; and when they are loosened, if it is cured with dry medicines that make pus, and with tourniquets, until it heals; and if without a cut of the artery as you work, hurry to cover it with cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze it with your hand so that the blood does not flow out; and if you do not have this, place your finger on the area until it becomes frozen, and moisten the area with cold water and squeeze it as needed; and those that are swollen and heavier in the extraction of the artery should be cauterized with this sharp cautery cutting .5 inches deep, but they should be thick for a longer time to preserve their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the strumens are too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two cuts, one being large in space; and when you have marked the two places, and you put hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and pierce the vein in two places; and they should be separated by the two heads because it is not bonded with this cautery throughout; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	And the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing into the veins that are on top of the head of the fire, and it does not help with any medicine that is applied there, and you see the patient writhing in pain, and feel the forehead trembling like a fever; and if they are weak and moist so that the hair of the scalp falls out, and the scalp becomes scorched from the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And they will call it the ancient "contused cure", and you should do this to the patient who has this illness on his forehead. Then you make three cuts evenly along the length of the forehead; one of the cuts is as deep as needed, advancing all the way from the brow to the root of the nose, and the other two are along each eyebrow above the eyelids, taking care not to cut the arteries that are at the top of the eyebrows. Also, keep your hand away from the continuation of the jaws, and let each wound be the size of three fingers joined together; and have a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth ready to clean and drain the blood, then insert the sharp spatula twice the width of what is shown here in its shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is through the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the skull that is between the two cuts down to the scalp, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this pointed instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Push the instrument called "culter-like" into the first incision. It is very sharp from one side, but soft and not sharp from the other, and it has the shape of a:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And press the cutting edge towards the raw flesh and the ribcage until it reaches the middle cleft, and push so that it comes to the midriff bone.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the veins that descend from the head of the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where it opens the midriff, and then continue in the middle cleft on the other side; and then drain the blood evenly, and press the leek for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton in each cleft, and put on moistened linen cloths soaked in vinegar, oil, and rosewater, and make sure that no pus comes into it; and on the third day, undo the sutures, and apply a large plaster of strong mustard, then treat with ointment of basilicon with oil of roses, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyelids
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with an acute catarrh usually, and you see the eyes becoming swollen and small, and the vision blurred, and burned papers; and the hair falls out, and a headache occurs at pain ague, and the patient coughs; then recognize these symptoms that those matters and such catarrh do not come from any other place than many veins, and the medicine to cure it is that.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you instruct the patient to bend their head back, then make a large cut across the forehead and another deep one below the ear.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 Start from the left temple to the right temple and let the incision reach the bone; move your hand away from the nerves that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the cut and put old cotton in between, and tie it with linen; then cover it with damp cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, and be careful not to get an abscess hot; once it is removed, you should rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat with things that are drying, which cause char to grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; administer it to these wounds to promote the growth of char everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones or similar items like iron; seeds, beans, peas; or flowing matter such as water and sand and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear stone or any other thing that does not align with the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see a stone, apply some drops of purple oil or camphor oil, then perform extraction; and make it vomit with mustard, and stop up the nostrils when the vomiting comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the head elevated.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often farting occurs through this treatment; and if it does not fart, extraction is performed with fine tweezers, of which the following is the procedure:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out at the hinges, that's good; if not, introduce extraction with a thin hook of double curvature; and if it doesn't jump out by that means, make a wooden pin and push its head into the hole of the ear strongly, stop up that which is around the pin with soft wax so that the air cannot enter with the pin; then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out in this way as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this manner, take some glue from it and take the birds, and put any tool sharp for that purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the glue on the stone or something else, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it doesn't jump out due to all the things that we have mentioned, hasten to make an incision in the ear so that pus and spasm come out; and the manner of the incision is such that you first lance the patient's head, drain the blood according to the measure of its power, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or tissue dependent on it; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, until you reach the bone, then pull it out as much as possible, and suck the pus quickly to your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a thin, slender spatula in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist from ear moisture, until you have made many slices; then extract it with subtle tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore, in water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use warm water and cotton wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie down with the same ear on that side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out because of this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it doesn't jump out, take many pebbles according to the width of your finger and lightweight, heat them slightly in the fire; then make the patient put a cord or stick in his ear, and hold one stone with the other hand from the other side, and press another stone against the stone that is in the ear; and keep pressing the stones together until the water comes out entirely, and then it will jump out completely; and if you see, take the cord, and push one of the stones further into the ear, and let the other end grab fire until the closest part is burnt; then remove all the stones as described in the pebble.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of an animal, if it is small like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large and can be felt, perform extraction with tweezers. This is the easier thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and the treatment of distillations, and if the cure does not benefit, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, take them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the string of which this form is given.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it shall be narrow beneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And the finest head should be inserted into the ear according to the amount of pain of the patient, then suck it completely at once; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, stop up the canal with cotton as I have said in the other chapter; and if they still do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations which the ancients have proven effective for worms, and you will find them or how to prepare distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all this equipment, thus is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make it narrow within and wide above with a silver or iron frame having one small hole, and over it a cover for the distillation; and to press inside the distillation, use one apparatus of iron well made for this purpose; and if you see that you need a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip, then put your oil or juice and any medicines in the string, which should be in the ear; then insert the scraper with all the cotton into the ear, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or the ear becomes warm; let the patient smell it within, and make sure the distillation is heated to about the same temperature as when it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicines will not be effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some deafness in the ears; and this same thing happens to men through stoppage of wounds or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes comes completely into the ear if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a little hole showing the deafness, which can easily be seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if the stoppage comes completely into the ear and cannot be seen, it is difficult to cure in many cases. In such case, you must put the sick person's ear in the sun and look inside. If you see a visible obstruction, you should open it with the spatula as shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and piercing in front and behind entirely, so that it does not prick the ear; if the inflammation is of flesh or bone of the ear, then hold it with subtle tweezers and strike gently until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the swelling has filled the ear entirely, take a subtle razor lightly and heat it slightly over fire, then place it in the ear of the swelling.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the swelling that causes discomfort in the ear of the patient, make a small incision carefully and ensure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a tube according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a lining and moisten it in rosewater and powdered vitriol; if you see the ear swollen, then you must pull out the lining and insert another moistened linen made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling is removed; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And when bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and linen in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments to stop the bleeding which are either distilling methods.
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal from paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method by which hairs that are damp and dry come from paper. It is necessary to stretch them with pliers and tweezers, and then rub their roots with a copper spatula. Then place it on broken glass.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if the hair cannot be removed by pulling, cauterize it with subtle lenticular cautery, and after incision is useful. Many times they repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when the hairs are cauterized by fire, the roots burn and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the shingles
