Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, also for the evacuation of blood; but let it stay until it turns black, and then you will cut it open or it would burst by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover, but first check if the abscess has cooled down and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders should be healthy, and he opens his mouth and the sergeant takes hold between his hands, and presses the tongue under all the instrument, as follows; and it should be of silver or subtle iron like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the onion and thrust it into the abscess, and pull it upwards as far as you can; and pull out any foreign matter from there, afterwards strike with the instrument, in which form it appears similar to a hammer; and yet the head is bent, and one part is against another, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument, strike it with the pliers, in which form it appears similar to:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have the instrument, strike one of the abscesses, and then strike the other in the same manner; after making an incision, gargarize the patient with hot, sharp, and mild water, and when bleeding occurs, gargarize the patient with hot, or scorched pomegranate seeds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then let it heal until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses than the two appear in the throat, if they do, strike them accordingly as the two equal.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside the throat, to be specific, an abscess of small size; and I had carefully closed all her throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passageway, nor could she eat or drink, and would have died if she remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had to be drained twice through the two openings of the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 Therefore, I immediately thrust it into one of the openings, then pulled it forcefully and took out a large piece of bone; then I reset another opening in the other shoulder, and opened its mouth and pressed its tongue; afterwards, I thrust the bone again into these abscesses, and took a part of it out, and no more blood came out; and thus I led the woman to have water and then wine, and she continued to drink from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the cavity which I had emptied, so much that it became very large; then I trapped it and burned it inside the neck: thus it did not grow any more; and I left those parts alone, and may God do with them as He wishes after me.
de l’uve	I will treat a woman with an eye problem that was inside her eyeball, in other words, an inflammation of the eyelid; and it had grown very close all over the eyelid, so the woman could not open her eyes due to the swelling, and she could neither see nor blink, and would have gone blind if it lasted for a day or two. The inflammation had swollen so much that it had filled about two pouches inside the eyeball. Then I immediately lanced it once, then pulled out a large piece of pus; afterwards I opened another hole in the other side of the eyelid, and I held her eyelids open and pressed them against each other; after that, I lanced the inflammation again, took a part of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the growth of the inflammation was stopped for the woman, and she began to see again. The inflammation grew again and filled the space I had created, until it became very large; then I trapped it and cauterized it inside her eyeball: thus the growth of the inflammation was stopped; and I left those parts, and nothing more happened to them except that God did something with them afterwards.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the rectum protrudes towards the anus and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen and round, it is called "anus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscesses are eased and it is subtle, you must cut it; and if it is rounded and not long, and it is either red or dark colored, you must avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger over the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, in the manner that I have said, of its bladder and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert the finger into the anus, pull it out, and cut it at the places where I have said to make the incision in the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cover more than the natural limit of excess; for if you do so, it causes harm to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the second anus, and heal it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 If the patient is afraid to be covered, then it is necessary that you use an instrument for the cauterization of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery is sharp heat.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient places their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue against the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and hold it with hot live coal, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the tip of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the head of a hair or medication is put on a head, as the comb of a spoon, and the instrument is placed entirely over the medicine above the eye; and the patient lies on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, but not down the throat, and the blood; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it swell and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument all over the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and lie for four or five days. And if you have to start the cautery again with the medicine, renew it, and after the cautery, wash around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, clean what is around the medicine; and irrigate with cold water, and heal with gargarisms until it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not only cautery; if it is healed by fumigation according to this method, take camomile, yarrow, rue, and wormwood, and assemble them all or some of these in one pot, and put them inside, and boil it; the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one comb-like instrument as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be silver or tin, and let one of the heads be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is putrefied; afterwards repeat often, until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the abscess's appearance, for many things happen therein; and do not do anything else but at the decline of the abscess's heat.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 If this is not present (silver or tin), then take a canal and put an eggshell crack into the head of the patient so that his mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell crack does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and it is good treatment along with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it happens that a bone or fish spine enters the throat, or something similar; in such cases, you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all instruments so that you can see it move; and if it does not open by itself and is swallowed back into the throat, make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will be expelled through vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, a piece of cotton, a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you pull it out; and if it does not come out as described above, take a plank-like instrument in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the top so that it can enter the throat more easily, and hold the head up high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or the patient will choke, do not push the bone deeper; it is better for the patient to push the instrument, because it can move or the object is expelled; if they push it downward, you pull it out equally with the instrument until it is expelled.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the absence of medicine is the cure, as I said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the patient's throat in the sun, since you press his tongue with the instrument I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the pus, draw it out very slightly with a small knife or delicate tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if it does not work, take a heated iron and place it in the patient's throat, then apply or press down on the handle of the iron frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And make the patient drink water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in so that he drinks it, moving his throat with your hand frequently; and as soon as the pus feels the water, he should spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, you should suffumigate the patient with asafetida, in the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this repeatedly, for it will soon return.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of fumigation is to take a pot with charcoal, cover it with a cloth perforated in the middle, and place the head of the instrument within it; then pour your fumigation into it, and have the patient put the head of the tube in his mouth, close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes up to his nose; and now it should start, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation repeatedly; let the patient endure thirst, eat salty and oily food, and drink no water; then it will be necessary for it to come out with this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the wound, appears, when it can be seen, resembles curved tweezers for entering into the throat; and it has the appearance of a syringe beak, and it should have roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many resemble abscesses, according to what follows in this book from one and another, and they are different in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that one is similar, and of those which retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is by the lews (lymph nodes) that are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are different from those of the base, and abscesses in the swollen lymph nodes are different from those that come at joints, and each should be judged separately in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, as long as the head is matured according to its completion; and if there are those that need to be pierced when they are hard, and do not die according to their maturity, such as abscesses that come from joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near to joints and are left until they ripen around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may become corrupt, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 For if the abscess is near the main member and you delay the perforation until it has ripened, it will harm the main member; or if it is near the base, pierce it as soon as it has become ripe, but do not pierce an abscess without complete digestion, except for one that is near the base which cannot be entered and is narrow inside, and a fistula forms, and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforating the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the disappearance of the fever, and the decrease of the pain and redness, and the swelling and subsiding of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation sit lower than the abscess, and where it has started to open; and the perforation should be as long as the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal or without a covering.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those who are swollen, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a firm state, it is better to let the opening remain until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 If you pierce it before this time, the body will be flooded with the pus from it, and it will be filled with much filth; and there is danger of hardening the lips and plunging deeper into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess that has been pierced according to the size of the body, as required by the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small abscesses, small punctures; and large abscesses, large punctures, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where you must cover the wound and close it, when it has become as shriveled as a cloth, and is dead, it is necessary to do as for babies: and if there are such as have been cut into three angles, and if there are those which are closed like the wings of myrtle, like abscesses in joints; and if there are those where you make a round incision, and other similar ones and closures.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 For a person without a head, being an abscess on the surface, it should be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out part of it; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing incorrectly; do this many times gradually, until the pus is completely drawn out; similarly, if the patient is weak, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old and debilitated people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The sphincter occasionally twitches with the discharge of pus, which may accidentally cause death to the patient, and you should not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, proceed with great caution in this chapter, and when you have pierced the abscess, drain the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is large, bring linen or old cotton threads; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, you must pack in each one a thread so that they meet one another; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, you must fill it with old cotton or linen wool without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then open it, and heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and apply it, wet the cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, administer medicine and treatment, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is wintertime, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, then you must place warm towels and cloths moistened with wine and oil over them; and if it is summer, and the wounds are fleshy, then you must place cloths moistened with cold water and oil, or cold water and cool oil for up to three days, as we have said; then drain the abscess and let it heal, as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how to proceed with the treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	The sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses on the head, it is our custom that they are wrapped in bandages, just like the grape-picker's hand and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some large and similar ones where there is moisture, just like boils; and there are some hard and stony ones without any doubt that the arteries do not oppose.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of the neck is that you probe with all instruments called "entromissoire," so the form comes later, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they make a long incision over it.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is evacuated, scrape clean without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, because it returns quickly if left; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise in vinegar and linen, and use the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed by night will heal.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the lint, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know that it does not heal over; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess remains filled with pus, squeeze it according to this shape, longwise; and throw away your onions, and scrape off all the skin from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the pus from where it is located; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise treat the abscess if it is pus-filled and cut and heal as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And the incision on the abscess becomes softer, because it is full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And in some of these abscesses or head, there is no moisture, and among these was the abscess that I lanced or the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a thorny stone, rough and swollen, and could not break it; and if one had struck it with any tool, one would have made a wound just like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads coming from children's heads and the roots of ears, they should be opened for as long as necessary, depending on the situation, to let pus out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times this abscess occurs at the neck, under the jaw, and in the armpits, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and they are connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 Each scrofula is properly inside the ribs, like the neck and abscess of the head as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see in good condition and resembles the color of the body, silent from all sides and not connected to the neck or the artery or the duct, and not deep; it should be cut open from above, and the skin of each part should be peeled off, and place the two lips of the forceps on the edges, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw gently and slowly, and ensure that you do not cover a nerve or the vein, and it should not be sharp or cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and look carefully before covering what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you open the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to proceed, put vitriol powder into the wound or some powders that stop blood, hold the wound closed; leave it until the abscess subsides, let the wound become soft, and begin to discharge pus.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 When the wound has stopped bleeding, return to your work until it is completed; then look for signs of small scrofula, if any appear, cut and wash them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, do not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang out, without causing harm; then apply old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment to the wound, and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 If you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary to gather the two edges of the wound and sew them together since there will be no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 You must understand how to cover the root of it [the ailment], draw pus from it, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce there where the pus emerges; and pierce as before described, in a downward direction, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar items so that it destroys what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply an ointment made of enchanter's nightshade char until it heals.
de squinance	And for strangury (a difficult or painful urination), you must crush barley grain in wine and give it to drink, and add the juice of dried figs; this will ease the pain and make urination easier.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the size of the throat; however, I have never seen one do it in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinch, the incision of the throat called "epiglote" should be made; and no aid should be given by them, because all the veins and the opening of the sickness are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two almond-sized places.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the mouth, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three or four small openings through the center, between the third or the size of the opening depending on its thickness, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there should be no cartilage, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 If the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat all the way along, then cuts the cartilage as far as it reaches the chin; and removes the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the windpipe as we have said; and this has been demonstrated by the sectioning of the trachea that jumps through the broken place, and by the absence of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which doubt exists about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care, and close it entirely without damaging the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient has been judged dead and his spirit departed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then one should press on the epiglottis because the patient cannot cough, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and for this reason the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, which has passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A maiden took the knife and thrust it into her throat, piercing part of the windpipe's channel; I was summoned to heal her, but found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found blood flowing from it, but I realized that neither voice nor conduit could be heard or followed except through the throat, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastily sewed up the wound and healed it until she was well; but the maiden's voice remained hoarse, and she recovered afterward; because of this, I say that in such a situation, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like a bladder, and it is much more common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; where natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental is in two ways: one is similar to fatty tumors, and the other type is similar to an abscess that comes from the artery; and it should be feared, and you should not force it unless in the small one, and prove and examine everything at the opening: if you find it similar to fatty tissue, and it does not move at all, strike it like you would a tumor, and pull it completely out if there is any; and close it well, and cure it as necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the nose
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours exist, which I will describe all their resemblances; now it is necessary that I say the entire difference between a notch and an opening.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Dislocation is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the swelling has passed, then the fracture is complete, after which the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 A notch has no heat or fever or pain, and contains the sinus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a small opening and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either fatty or moist, and most are colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the cure of the knot, that you test and inquire first about every instrument which is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will come or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The manner of incising an abscess is that you take a place more moist than you find in the abscess and rub your fingers back and forth until you feel that the pus has broken through, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the pus-filled cavity, but be careful not to let it spurt.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs into the wound, let it be colored as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards no moisture comes out from the incision, know that it is filled with fat; then make a cross-shaped incision, take hold of it with forceps, lightly peel off the skin on both sides and draw out the cavity where it lies, making sure you remove it whole with the fat; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If anything remains, the pus returns repeatedly many times; if a little bit remains and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound and hold it closed with bandages, apply hot things to soothe the abscess, treat it with other cures until it heals completely; and if it is large, make two incisions at the edges of the wound, and heal the resulting raw flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is beating against you or something else, rush and use vitriol powder instead, let it lie for 2 to 4 days until the wound heals, and allow the boil of blood to rest; then return to cover what was left uncovered with linen.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of the probing instruments, and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three cross-shaped ones called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and there are also three types: large, medium, and small for encircling abscesses with fistula; and they are similar to needles used on witches, and made of citron wood, iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are more experienced in black plaster for encircling the edges of the fistula; and they are also in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wound's width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of tumors are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and some tumors have two humps in three ways; and some tumors have three humps, and are also of three types; and some tumors have two humps, and tumors with one hump only, and are also of three types; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The chisels used for this are sharp and should not be cut from any other part, so as to avoid the vein or nerve; and these instruments called intromissories are placed in the hands of the patient, so that he does not feel it at the opening of abscesses; and they come in three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one should not use any other but for charnu (charred or hardened) places such as legs, arms, breasts, and wounds, and sometimes another instrument similar to fistula drains is made, according to this shape, to bleed.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place that heals from veins and arteries, and sometimes it is returned in this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to corrupt, until they appear like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, should do so according to this form described in this line b. up to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then remove the fat, apply medicine to the wound using corroding char, then bring together the two lips of the wound for stitching, and cure it until it is healed; if the breast sinks downwards due to its large size as happens with women, bind them in two stays, by two similar cuts; from this one will hold the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b up to line g; then remove the skin between the two lips, extract the fat, and apply what has been mentioned for stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the cure, until it heals; if it does not heal or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest or due to the discharge of blood, you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and let it remain until it digests the remaining fat, then cure it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscess on the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are treated as hard scrofulas with swellings that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those containing moisture must be amputated according to this form, from line b up to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire hole that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as needed until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, make incisions as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound forms a hole, bring fire as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the cutting of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is injured and the skin above it thickens, there are often abscesses, and the same happens with a burst vein and an abscess; and if one recognizes this by the artery, then the abscess extends through the full extent; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels tightly constricted; and when it is due to the vein, it swells upwards appearing round; and it is foolish to amputate such an abscess, and especially when it is under the joints and angles, and in the neck and around other joints, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Therefore, the treatment with iron must be avoided for those at the head, and similarly for those who are swollen from artery; they should make an incision through the skin along the length; then open the wound in a circular manner, carefully separating the artery from the tendons, until it is exposed; then push an awl beneath it and pierce it until the other side, and tie the artery with double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries located in the temples; then press the area between the two ligaments with a probe until the swelling subsides, and separate the abscess; then apply the cure of heated iron bow, until the ligament bursts; then treat it with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed; if the abscess is due to a vein opening, you should mark with your hand all that can be seen of the abscess to the entire skin, then pierce the awl beneath the area held in your hand, and let it pierce through, taking care to leave two threads; then tie the abscess as I have said, or ligament of one of the two parts with double thread; if you doubt that the threads will not burst, you should insert another awl all along the thread beneath the abscess at the incision of the first awl, and pull out the threads in four places; then crush the abscess until the excess subsides, then crush the excess fat and leave what is tied; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, abscesses of the nerves occur when they are injured or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this often happens in the shoulder and the thigh, and in all places where there are joints, and it is called a serious abscess, and its color resembles that of the body, and it occurs in various dispositions with pain; and when it is pressed strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not completely within the body, but under the skin; and it is quite silent from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, neither up nor down, and one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps contraction will occur; and one who is on the head or forehead, let the skin be spatulated.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, take tweezers and press it at its root; and if it is large, open it with an incision, peel off the skin, then cut open the bone and close the wound by stitching, and let it heal until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Hanging large swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; some are small and others very large; I have seen a man who had two bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were slit open, and moisture continuously ran out.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed and found one of them to weigh eighteen ounces, and the other six pounds, and when you make an incision in it, you can see that the patient is moist, and the color of the intestine is pale and wet with a fine root; if you cut it open with a broad spatula, be sure the fire cautery is present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For at the thigh often comes too great discharges of blood, and if it threatens you, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and terrified of the incision with iron, take a thread well made, and tie it as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread of plumb until it stops the flow, and shrinks by it; and if the roots are large, be careful to cope with it yourself, but you can well cope with half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not copier the thread which is of dark color and of poor sensation and of milky eye.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this abscess hardened, and I will come to the treatment of leprosy hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of the wound or rupture of the sifac, and it is on the stomach and in some of the buboes, as happens in other routes, or from blood that leaks from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind-inflammation; and if this is through the sifac route and from the opening of the buboe, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	and if it is from the intestine, then it is more varied, and when it is pressed with the fingers, it sinks back in, and then returns, and sometimes it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and through great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and easily opened when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and filled according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to wind-inflammation, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery or vein, or wind-inflammation.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary that you let the treatment be.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the belly, you must instruct the patient to fasten his anus, and extend himself straight, then sign all around the belly; then command him to press himself gently between your hands, then go around the area that you have signed with a spatula, then cut half of the abscess above with a large spoon; then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk and let the wound heal by itself; then open half of the incised abscess over the suture, and insert your finger and search for the intestine; if you find it tied by the suture, untie it, and push the intestine out of the abdomen; and if you find a belly button, take it with the spoon, and cut away the excess; and if the artery opposes or the vein, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert them through the holes that you have made, and tie the abscess around with them in a cross shape that you are making perforate; then hold the abscess closed in four leagues above the needles, and if you see it open, remove the needles, and let the wound heal until it can close by itself, and cut away the dead flesh when it becomes soft and can be cut, then cure the wound as necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; and drain the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the area as necessary, and stitch the area.
dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of a sore and how to treat it with medicines and when to use iron cure; now let us say what a sore is like in marriage, and great caution should be taken in its treatment, and the ancients said that when sores are in places where they can be shaved like sores that occur in mammary glands and thighs, and similar places, it must be completely removed when it begins; but when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal it; no one has ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when they are in place and can be removed as we have said, it is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him purge if he has obvious fullness, then prepare the patient. That is, shave the area where the operation will take place; then pour boiling oil or other hot substance over the wound, and let all pus flow out; leave no bone or cartilage unbroken; and let all blood flow freely. And press well on the area with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood opposes the incision of an artery or a vein, cauterize it until the wound is closed; then heal it with other treatment until it heals.
de ydropisie	of the hydropieric disease
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have already said in the division the resemblance of edema, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is done with medicines, and that which is cured with iron: only this is excreted; it should not be touched by iron in these two resemblances: namely, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this resemblance of edema called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak or has another disease besides edema, such as dropsy of the belly and similar things; do not touch iron in that case because there is doubt. However, if you see the patient strong and he has no other disease except edema only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then act thus: lift the patient straight onto your hands, and the attendant presses the belly outward bringing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the curved spatula according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And to make an incision in the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And it should not be so deep that it reaches the intestines when it is pushed in, and it must not be pierced; then check if the yolk-sac is adhered to the intestines: if this is the case, you must make an incision below the navel three fingers right of the nipple; and if the yolk-sac is due to liver disease, it should be made on the left side of the navel three fingers; and if it is due to the swelling, it should be on the right, and the patient must not lie on the incision so that the fluids do not run to the weak place; then pierce the skin with the instrument, push it, and withdraw your hand as much as the spatula between the skin and the sac, as when peeling an apple or something similar in quantity; then pierce the sac until the spatula reaches the watery place, and this is the amniotic fluid, then draw it out, and insert this instrument where it was described earlier:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and made of lead or light iron, and in the lower part, there are small holes; on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head of the shoulder is cut like a quill, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes make for carving a quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.
