Above the head is the anvil, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends now on the instrument; empty then the space of half or one third part, because if you empty too much at that time, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he falls to the ground, or approaches death; but empty according to its strength, and according to what the dispositions of his strength indicate about the patient and his pulse; then draw the instrument and stop the water, it is now held due to the cauterization that closes the hole that I spoke about, that you make holes in this way; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering, and drain a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to wait too long but only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you have doubt about the patient, and you leave him much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and anoint him with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is dry, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the removal of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 There are times when children are born who have no foreskin or the foreskin is small or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to pierce through the sponge-like substance very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then put the subtle foreskin of wood (clo) in place, and hold it and keep it for three or four days until he wants to urinate, if the opening is removed then let him urinate, and then replace it; and in case there is no need, because the urine that comes out does not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 For the one whose ulcer is small, it is treated with a cloth of plugged-up wool, as we have said, it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those without ulcers in their place are blessed, for no one is born with an ulcer on the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before tying up the penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the marris, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of work is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the penis and the buttocks at the same level, so that the testicle falls into the scrotum as required; and guard against excessive bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from the wound, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis ulcers
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathe appears on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly sores; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must pick them up once a week with a thin instrument, cut and clean them all, then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on top; then treat it with diaphinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the anus is malignant (unhealthy), with pus-like discharge, then you must bring fire cure.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cauterized (burned), and if the anus is in a swollen state around the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then first remove the swollen anus that is inside; and when it heals, treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you treat it together, the testicles are not completely assured that they will not be punctured, and there comes blackness and corruption in its sheath and area; then everything that is black and corrupted must be cut away, and then lay it on a plaster of honey and flour made from the peel of pomegranates and other things, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if a discharge of blood comes out, apply the lunar cautery in this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery also helps in these conditions: that is, discharge of blood and corruption; and if the testicles of the penis are corrupted and retracted, then you must insert or cause a canal made of wood from the plum tree, and make the patient urinate; and when the skin reaches the tip of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised or it occurs due to injury or abscess, then you must shave the hair with an instrument suitable for the task, until the ligaments are loosened, and release the testicles from all sides; and if this is difficult to discuss, then you must shave it at the spatula a little way along the penis and skin; then press gently between them, and put a thin linen cloth damp with cold water on it, so that it does not stick.
de la circoncision	of circumcision (when referring to the surgical procedure)
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not without reason and similar to other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will and specifically on infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one day and all at once; however, there were those who feared it because there are two layers, and by chance if one above is cut, the one below may remain.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the coping is covered, and the pain is doubled; and at the circumcision of the tip of the member, it is not certain that the point of the tool touches the member; and by chance, the iron may slip during the circumcision of the nail, and ruin the work, and many times they are born without need for circumcision, and I have wanted this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the amputation which is made at the joint of the limb I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, cut it evenly all the way through; but let the veins be well narrowed around the skin; and let the method of the first operation be that you make the child think, if he understands, that you tie the thread only around the rod, and then let him rest in every possible way that you can; then let it be between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then push your hand to the rod and blow or cut, and pull it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the filth that has gathered there, then tie the ligature with a double thread, then tie below the knot to another knot; and hold it at the second knot by the cocket and index finger, and cut between the two knots, then untie the knot quickly and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow freely, for this is the purification; and put powder on it and powdered egg white glues from a half-cooked egg tempered with rose water, confectioned with fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and heal it with another healing as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for healing is as follows: the two shoulders should be tender and should be cut, and they should also be as large as the fist equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of healing is when the flesh within is cut open; therefore, it must be stretched with the nail, so that the joint becomes abscessed; and equalize it, and if you cannot hold it with the nail, use pliers, and then equalize it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and that which is beneath the worm [abscess] is swollen, let it be left until the abscess subsides, and gently lance it; if it bursts as you can move it, do not injure the part of the worm, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure the place with powder, as we have said treating powders, and if it bursts excessively, and goes above, it will not harm; so cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is caused by a stone, frozen blood, pus, or mucus (which we have mentioned in the division); and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone lodged at the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be bent over his knees; his feet should be placed on the back, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part above the lower back, and restrain the patient as much as possible; and then you should forcefully press the neck of the bladder to express the stone above it, so that the urine is released. And if it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must provide extraction using an instrument called "siringue", which has the following form: made of subtle, light silver tube like a bird's feather; and the cannula should be one and a half palm lengths long, and it should be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the method of the issue of the urine is that you take a double thread, tie it to the end of a cotton or linen string, and push the string into the syringe; remove any excess thread and push it up to the tip of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and dip the tip in egg white and olive oil and warm water; then make the patient sit on the chair, anoint the bladder and penis with oiled moistened cloths; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the anus; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and the patient should feel it reaching the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide through which it goes is twisted; then tie the thread to the entire string and the urine will follow the string, then remove it and straighten the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Illness of the bladder (or urinary system)
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	For scorchings or blood coming into the bladder (or urinary system), or pus is gathered there, and you see it distill acids and medicines, do all the instruments that are called "clepsydra" (hydrotherapy device). The shape is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the medicines are put into the correct position so that they can stop the swelling without adding anything, if it is possible to draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you wish to empty your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and draw while pulling; if you draw out the moisture with the syringe, then forcefully push the plunger in; it will enter, and go to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it; this is the form of the subtle clisterium used to clisterize the bladder: this is it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or iron, and the head [of the shoulder] is higher; and beneath lies the breast or the joints fall; then take a mutton bladder and fill it with the moisture that you use to soften the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread; heat the bladder filled with moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the plaster into the bladder, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture contained within, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, pierce it roundly; then forcefully insert the thread through these holes, assemble the circle like a thimble, fill it with oil and moisture and water, place it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division of stones the methods and extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone implanted in the rain and all the signs, and in what stone one should operate according to size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder resembling water in its subtlety; it opens a passage, enlarges the patient's urine channel, and pierces it many times, then ties it up; and many foundations occur because of these jumps; and children's healing is light until they are four years old, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is in the middle, for those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For sometimes it blocks the stone from being extracted.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take hold of the patient by the feet, and push down and move him below, so that the stone comes out to the front of the bladder and protrudes somewhat from the opening; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining towards the bottom; then press and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall to the touch of all [the body], wet your finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is an infant, or you may use a tool, if the patient is an adult; and push it into its foundation, seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, squeeze it at the neck of the bladder; then press upward with your finger, and push it out where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press the kidney with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then put the spatula covering it, so that it forms:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And between the coccyx and the foundation, do not dig it out but on the left side of the anus; and let it be straight above the stone, and your fingers should be at its foundation or at the top, and let it be cut through crosswise so that it is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps you press too hard on the finger which is at its foundation, causing it to jump out suddenly; and know that there may be several stones or angles and edges; if there are many small ones like a bean, round and smooth, then it is easier to remove.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 To the one who has an angle or corner, make the incision larger; and if it does not burst open, you must pull upwards with pliers that resemble a saw at the tip, to forcefully dislocate the stone so it doesn't escape; or push in instruments of subtle curvature beneath the tip; and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, widen the small hole slightly, and if it is not yet broken, apply vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, push first on the largest at the bladder's neck, then strike, pull hard, and deal with the smaller ones afterward if there are any more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For the patient, there are two things that may happen: either he dies or urine comes out constantly because the loins cannot be joined; but despite this, you should try to draw or break with pliers as much as possible while pulling it apart; and when you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and tighten it, and cover with a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and cold rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess heat; then make the patient lie on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you undo it (the bandage), wash well the wound with oil and water, then apply the ointment of defyfinicon and the ointment of basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 If abscesses and corrosions come in the wound and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained because without urinating; then press your foot on the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder and corrupt it; then wash the wound with water and oils and linen, and help him in every way you know, until it heals; and it is necessary that all the hours you heal it, you bind the two thighs together and put the medicines on the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and it is guided by the rod and thrust in, and urine cannot be expelled; heal this as follows: you should cut many times, but take care not to cut too deeply due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have previously experienced it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and with four angles pierced in one thorn:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then push the auger gently into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the auger in the stone slowly, bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from another side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what is held back within the rod from the stone.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and jumps with urine, the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this due to any obstacle, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then insert the rod towards the stone between the two ligaments, pull it out, release the ligament, clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens rarely that a stone enters a woman, and if it ever occurs, the cure is severe, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to examine herself, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is when it happens that one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deeply lodged than the stone of the man, therefore it requires a deeper incision, and great fear is involved. If such a situation arises, you must take a midwife skilled in the art, if one cannot be found easily, then choose a subtle caste midwife; and present her a wise bailiff in the affairs of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and order her to perform what you command regarding the incision of the stone; and make sure that the woman is a virgin: then you must push your thumb or foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, you should hold it with your thumb, and order her to press her left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is found, you must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike above the stone in the root of the thigh near the middle of the bone, where the stone is moved to appear, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your finger on top or below the stone, and let it be cut off at first small [amount]; then push the flesh into the cut, if you feel the stone is close enough to open the wound, and know that there are many kinds of stones: such as small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 Know the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 If it bleeds continuously, apply powdered vitriol and hold for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone is expelled, and have tools as I told you in removing the stone from men to assist you in your task; and if it continues to bleed, and it is of the artery that was cut, apply powder over the area and bind with straps and bandages, and do not attempt again, for there is danger that the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wounds have closed, return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	of soft hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquose is not something other than an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called "white pus", and sometimes it is properly within the egg's membrane, if one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the white pus that we have said, and this does not occur unless there is a rupture.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this accumulation is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there comes a blow to the kidneys, and this moisture appears in various colors: either a color declining to yellow, or without red, black, or white, and this happens more frequently; and these are signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white like we have said, it is an abscess, and it grows long as the figure of an egg, and do not open the kidneys, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the cloth, the abscesses are caused with a part of the egg, and because of this it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the hide of hocks and the white yolk, one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe it thoroughly, from which the form is as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, the one who comes after the incision judges what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be anesthetized to our power and the filling of his body; then he lies on his back, on something slightly elevated, and put many layers of cloth beneath him; then lie on his left side, and command the assistant to stand on the right, and stretch the arm at one of the two ribs nearest the hocks; then take the cautery iron, strike the hide of the hocks along its length down to the bone, and make your incision straight in describing the hide of the hocks up to the white yolk, and peel it off delicately according to our power; then pierce the yolk completely with water and drain all the water, and then put your onions, and close the yolk; and do not touch the bone, but only the yolk; strike all around it carefully, if you do not strike it skillfully, the water will return; and if the egg bursts during your work, repair it in its place when you have completed the work of the yolk; then bring together the two leaves of the hide of the hocks into a stitch, then treat it like other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted with some other disease, you must tie the vessels that are suspended, taking care of the discharge of blood; then cut the kidney and remove the bladder, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts together, know that they are two branches; if you strike the other part as you have done the first equally, then suck out the blood, and place damp linen in oil of roses on it; and place another damp linen in wine and oil on the other side, and place two stones on it, and cover with doubled cloths, and tie it all together with a suture according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two pieces of cloth, and use damp linen like this shape and sew them together in the girdle of the arms, and one of the shoulders takes it up to the bottom, and the other at the hilt part; and the other shoulder on the opposite angle, and gather all together in the knot of the arm band; and sometimes the cautery ramie is used instead of iron cutting, and you take a subtle cautery tool, strike the skin of the shoulders, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus containing the ulcer is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce the exposed pus with it, and peel off the skin using this hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cup in all ways that you can, as long as it heats up; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg (yolk); and know that this work is more effective; and beware of discharge of blood, and be aware that the works of cutting; and if anything happens contrary to this, or abscess erupts or discharge of blood or something else, cure what happens contrary to it, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is afraid and does not wish to undergo this procedure due to its horribleness, then perform perforation, as I have told you, and know that when you are certain by the signs we have said that the abscess is located there, you should make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the area below the entire spatula's width, and insert the perforation along the length of the body; let the wounds be wide enough for all the pus to flow out; then place cotton over the area, hold it in place, and allow the remaining pus to drain; then cure the wound until it is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to escape from the opening of the wound, you must apply a feather or the instrument used to treat dropsy, as its form has been described earlier; enlarge the wound's opening, know that the pus will return, and be aware that it is collected after six months or more, and when it is collected as described earlier, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the cheeks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the section of this [medical] procedure, there is fear in many cases, so it seems more appropriate to leave it [the procedure]; and I will tell you the work and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the body, especially in the bowels; and this happens often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 By excessive sour and acute fluid that is spread in the lungs, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body; and no pain is found, and it is a painful abscess; and perhaps there are some abscesses swollen with pus and hard, of this color, and sometimes it comes from an artery, or swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from an artery, it can be known by the color of the abscess hot, when you press on it with your hands; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 One who is swollen with the vein is recognized by his disposition at the expression of the fingers, and can well make an incision on this resemblance, and on other things; it is that you cut the flesh of the hump, then the egg is above, and the yolk flows out white, and deliver the suspensorium from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already boiled with these things born, then you must draw out the egg and chop it; if it is raw or inside the vessels, where it is within the bladder, you must deliver all that tender stuff and chop it.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the pimple is hidden inward, you should cut it all and remove the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply linen cloth wet with rose oil and wine to the wound, then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the cheeks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enveloped by an envelope resembling a boil, with the softening of the fingers, and the patient groans heavily as he goes; and the cure for this disease is extremely dangerous like the one before, and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 You must make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspension device for the eyes below his feet, against all the vessels close to the vein, and mark them with the master; then stretch them out fully. Then you cut into the artery sharply wide through the vessels until they are exposed, and then peel off from both sides, as we have said in the extraction of the temples' arteries; then insert a double-threaded needle and tie it to the first point where the blood has flowed, and tie it directly to the other end; then pierce it in the middle straightly according to the length of the body, and drain out the corrupted fluids; then treat the wound as you would a bowel injury, so that no vessels burst from one of the eyes; because there is no harm in this, but if all the vessels burst, you must withdraw the eyes from all the vessels; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot heal.
de la routure dou syfac	of the dislocation of the thigh
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The appearance of this hernia is through an opening that comes from the incision or extension on the abdomen in the area of the inguinal region, so that the intestines descend from that rupture towards one of the corners; and this rupture is either due to the incision or the extension of it, and these two types of causes may occur for various reasons: either by impact, jump, strain, lifting of heavy objects, etc., and similar things; and the signs that it is an extension of the inguinal hernia are that it occurs gradually, over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal in size up to the full extent, because the hernia follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the incision of the intestine, which causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin near, and this is due to the rupture of the internal organs and the body going into shock due to the incision.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are twisted with it and held in place, causing great pain to suffer by the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, fear is present, so one must escape from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	1. And the manner of work is that you command the patient to pull out the intestine with their hand from inside through the wound, if it can be inserted; then hold its neck between your hands, and lift the thighs; then position the blade above, and cut all the hide of the shoulders long; then push into the hollows of the waist bones according to what is needed for opening the wound, and make them such that the eyes can come out; then scrape the fat that is under the hide of the shoulders, until the white fat becomes completely exposed from all sides; then put your index finger where the shoulder bone is, in the place that is between the white fat that is under the hide of the egg, and the second fat, and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second fat; and move your hand to the right inside the shoulder blade, and position the white fat on your left hand, and lift the egg towards the belly with all the fat towards the waist; and command the assistant to stretch the egg upward, and loosen what is in front behind the ligament; and check with your fingers if any intestine is enveloped or hard white fat, and if you find anything, put it in the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and put it in the back part of the fat, which is after the hide of the shoulders; after the waist, then pierce the bones that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the fat, which we have said is under the hide of the shoulders, with a strong rope of two parts; then wrap the bones with the threads, and tie them in two parts, so that no vassals who feed them can enter into it, unless the abscess does not come out; and place the rope according to the first rope length, and after these two ropes leave the fat that is under the shoulder blade to be large by one finger width; and after all that, shape according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part that is under the hide of the shoulders, as much as it will allow, and curve it, as we have said above; then bring moistened linen into oil and put it on the wounds, and place the rope that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white pustules are cauterized as we have said before, after incising, due to fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 This often happens and leave the ligament until it chooses to come out by itself; if it delays in falling off, you should irrigate it with hot water, and apply as we have said, until it comes out; then treat the wound from another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of soft hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I never saw anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like the graft which is joined with the bone, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after cutting them lightly on top of it; then break it in the middle, and treat the abscess from those who work on it, until the vessels come out; and treat it as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes it comes about in an abscess as we have said, and open the hole; do not draw out any of the intestines with the feces, and if there is some drawn out, it is a mistake and repair it every hour; and yet if it stays too long in this spot, the wound or fistula grows, until the intestine is drawn out; this happens due to the extension of the fistula which is in the abscess, as we have said, for it is extended, then becomes softened and swollen the hole and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies down supervised on his back between your hands, then break the swollen abscess hole from side to side according to the thickness of three fingers; and then extract the fistula which is under the skin that surrounds it, then take the rod and put it over the visible part of the fistula; and press it to the stomach, then stretch the two visible parts of the fistula on the head of the rod, and press them both; then extract the head of the rod, and do not cover or extend the fistula or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the graft of the intestines; then treat it by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, if it is punctured and cures the wound, let it heal while it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The siphon is constricted, without any appearance in the opening, and the cauteries are moved closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the cheeks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin on the cheeks becomes soft in some men, because the charms that are inside are softened and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one sees it needs to be cured, to make the patient lie on their back, and to cut the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then bring the two lips together at a stitch, and if you see, sew first the excess skin that has been softened at 2 or 4 strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and the wound is cured as other wounds, until it heals, and sew the thread.
dou chastrement	the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that charms are mentioned in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: the first is that mirrors in a charm respond when asked and provide a cure; and the second, because we often have need of castration of certain animals to aid us, such as cows, sheep, goats, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, charms are done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting (or slitting).
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the case of the charm by attraction, we sit the animal in hot water until its genitals are softened and relaxed; then we take hold of it with our hand, keeping it restrained until it is calmed and no longer feels anything.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For the branding of size: you must mark the beast, and press the hide of the cheeks with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike each ear with the brand when they are well scorched; leave any small spot unbranded and the subtle one that is on the vessel; and this kind of branding is dried out rather than the one made by attraction, because at the attraction something from the cheeks may remain, which causes the beast to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is according to two types of men: one in which there is an opening between the two cheeks as the figure of woman's nature, having hair and sometimes it urinates in court.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And another way is in women, and it has above the penis as a rod, and they copulate.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment of the man and woman is that you copulate the joined genitals all, and heal them as other wounds; in another way, from men whose urine jumps through the skin of the penis, there is no healing.
de la tentigene	the treatment
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tension is a joined genital on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have one as large as a hand, and this is healing.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You must dye the excess of the tension with your hand or onions and copulate lightly; do not go too far in as it may cause bleeding, then heal it with other remedies until it is healed; and another character that comes from the wife's mouth, and is pushed out, and sometimes jumps violently, and resembles a cow, and because of this, they call it "the disease of cows" by the ancients.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It is necessary that you cut [it], as we have said before, and treat it until it heals.
de erratique	Of a dislocation
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 If the nature of woman is not detected, or it is small, and its nature is either by birth or accident due to illness that comes in; or it is by artificial means such as a charm or subtle or thick syrup, and it is made completely within marriage, or outside, or whether it is; and they must prevent conception, delivery, and avoid the flowers having [the child]; and this knowledge can be determined by observing the vaginal discharge.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the stoppage is close to appearing, either at your hand or eye.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is by subtle syrup and the stoppage is close to the liver, hasten and do this: put your two index fingers together and the woman should be lying on her back with her legs spread; then form the two livers, so that the subtle syrup is rounded, and cover the stoppage; then take linen and moisten it in oil, and place it on the area, and let the woman lie there each day until she does not conceive.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the dislocated joint is hard and thick, you should cut it with a chisel resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocated joint is made of flesh, suspend it with a rope and cut it; have prepared medicines that stop blood, such as hog's lard, dragon's blood, incense, together with many eggs; then bring a large bandage, so that the wound cannot heal; and let it remain long, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when flesh comes in the wound (or abscess), it should be covered in this manner, unless the abscess is inflamed.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an abscess swollen at the marriage (joint), one must not do anything to it.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins without the cort (cortex) treatment, and when hemorrhoids become old, they swell; and we have said in the division what they look like, their signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and the swelling, when they are completely in the joint (maris), and do not appear to touch, should not be treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those at the mouth of the joint can be felt, these are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore you should put the woman in a cold house, then pull out the swelling with pliers at its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicine that stops bleeding such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet to the opening for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding comes forth, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and grape bark and ivy leaves and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it bleeds, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not bleed, make him (the patient) lie face down and the armpits should be wounded; then take linen, wet it in the juice of plantain or elder with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess has rested, treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" should be red and resemble a rough chief, if necessary cover it as I have said in the text; and then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	"of the anus abscesses"
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many forms of abscess come in the marriage, such as boils, pus-filled abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore, in this treatment, it is necessary for me to describe the abscess that appears in marriage, which is not one of those that swell; and if you want to know the work of iron, observe whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, and filled with heat and fever, and if it turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Do not rush to pierce it immediately, but let it heal as much as the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have two chairs where he can lean, and support his back and legs at the parts away from the leg; and let his knees be spread open, and place his arms under his thighs and tie them well with a good rope; then bring the pustule towards the right side, and bring the instrument used for opening the abscess, from which follows its shape; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, that you pierce the tip first to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not burn the patient; if the instruments are larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he places the horn of the instrument above, and marks the instrument.
