Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and one touches it with a soft hand, it must be covered with a poultice of lard; and when the boil is empty, you should put wet, oiled bandages in the wound, or green, dry, cooked poultices; and put the poultice edge from the wound to the full depth of the marrow, and put over the marrow and over the clean, oiled linen bandage soaked in vinegar or malvish that has been cooked; then cure it for two days after the application until it is healed; and sometimes lift the marrow and the wound with a poultice of vinegar and honey, and then with vinegar or long-cooked arnica or Aristolochia roots; then return to the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is healed over in the marine, you must avoid burning it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 Firstly, one must know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs when you see the woman straining downwards and desiring to urinate: then hasten the child to be born; now understand that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it issues from under the head, and follows with him; and when you see these signs, you must gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends above her head, then it follows with it, and the membranes of the womb are emptied of its superfluities through good cleansing; and this which comes in another way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Sometimes it happens over the limbs, and the torso or shoulders, or the hands, or over the abdomen, or back, and is turned accidentally around the neck, or in other malicious ways; therefore, it is necessary that the bailiff be wise and skillful in these matters, and aware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how to help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes down naturally towards its head and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the vital forces of the infant are weak, make her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the small spatula (spatumile) between her fingers as shown in the figure:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And cut the second rib, and strike at its nail until the moisture that is within it comes out; and grasp the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must fumigate the woman with mustard seed oil of sage; then make her take and vomit of castor oil, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour; now the child will descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 If the two hands come out, it is necessary that you reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot be put back in, place the woman on the chair, and lift her legs up; then tip the chair onto the ground, and bind the woman so she does not scream during the process; and if the hands still cannot be put back in, and the child dies, cut open the mother's belly with the knife placed before, extract the child, and reset again.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 The birth of the child is on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out on its feet, you must push it upwards; and then gradually turn it, until it is level; then take one of the feet and stretch it gently, bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 It cannot jump up to any knees, if it commands to catch it, and makes it vomit with the throat-constriction; if it leaps away, may it be so if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Thus it should be done gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not come away as we have, say that you take musk-juice from the altar and oil of sage, and melted pitch, and grind all in the mortar; then put the nature of a woman inside this ointment and apply it externally on the place; then make her sit in hot bath up to her chest; and when she is softened below, let him tie her with mirrr-gauze and place it under, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the chair, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and press her stomach gently, for the infant jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the infant comes in this form, place the child's hands palm to palm; then support its head on its neck, and hang its legs downwards, and lay it on the bed; fold its hands palm to palm, and then hold its hands above its belly, and push its hips out, until it is aligned below; if the infant does not slide, take its feet and straighten them, then straighten its belly upward, then put your hands; rock the baby gently, and command the woman to seize herself until the infant is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the emergence of the child which comes out one hand wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to find a way to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then lift the woman and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed and spread her legs widely; then apply the mustard plaster that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then study how to bring back the hand; and deliver the baby according to its natural shape, make her vomit, and command her to seize herself until the infant is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	The issue of the child on its neck, and it has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the servant holds his hand, then turns it bit by bit and pulls it gently; and when it is even, place natural muscle balm of high altitude and oil on it, as we have said, then command him to move it bit by bit; and when you have done this, make him sit on the chair, and command him to grab it; and make him vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner, treat everything else.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the child comes forth in this manner completely, you strike the afterbirth on your nail until the moisture is evacuated; and if the placenta rises to its place and to its neck, you strike it so that it is not retained and the placenta dies; then push the child down as far as you need to, and command the woman to grab it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins   (or from twin pregnancy)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born often and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange and rarely happens.   (It is common for twins to be born, but it is rare for more than two to be born at once.)
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange things, and do not live unless named; I know them, as they can multiply themselves, and are driven away by the one who invented them, which is linked to filth; and sometimes they come out naturally like worms, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out violently, treat them as we have said, and let the balm be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do as much as is needed to heal it.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the marriage of one to two or three or four or five or six, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise healer; it is necessary that the balm knows this, for sometimes similar things happen; do as needed according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you care for the woman in labor with a dead child or an empty womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to manual work; then you must know if the woman is of pure virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should lie on her back, and her chest inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the attendant should strain her with both hands, or tie her to the bed so she is not treated in the removal of the child; then anoint the mouth of the dead child with moist oils mixed with musk, aloe, and flax seeds, then anoint the attendant's hands with these oils and these musks; then insert them gently into the dead child's mouth, ensuring that they reach the desired location, and be careful if the anus is exposed as it should descend on the head; then pierce the anus in the eyes or neck or mouth or palate or below the beard or in the forehead or near the sides or near the costal region, and if the expulsion is from the feet, then pierce or press them gently at the middle of the ribs; and you should hold the anus with your right hand, and place the horn between your left-hand fingers, and insert it fully into any of the locations mentioned above, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the anus:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then drive it against the other one, whichever is needed, so that the extraction is equal; and then adjust it equally by moving from both sides to make them move out, and keep the ends pointed for movement, as in the figure below:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 If part remains, then press one of your thumbs against oil and push into that part while pulling the other; if no part remains, place the splint higher up the limb and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 If one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be returned due to the tension, then you should wrap it with a cloth until it comes out completely; then break it at the joint of the sole or at the toe, and do this for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is narrow in the birth passage, or if there is a sharp assembly of the skull, you must insert the pointed sponge between your fingers, and make the skull open and extract the water; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and in the same manner do for the child naturally swollen; then pull the bones apart with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it is held back by force, it should be cut, until the moisture which is in a worse position issues; and if it cannot issue, hit it with pieces as hard as you can. And if it is inflated in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is swollen above its feet, the treatment is light and the repositioning to the mouth of the bladder is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is protruding in the abdomen or the anus, you must push it back into place covered with a cloth over your hand; and with the abdomen or anus, press until the moisture that is there corrects itself; and if another member has been dislocated, and the head remains, you must put the thumb of one hand inside the vagina, and guide it until the opening of the vagina; then you put in your index finger or middle finger and guide it further; and if the opening of the vagina is narrowed due to abscess that has come, you should not push, instead you should administer moist and greasy things; and you should administer ointments, and oil in warm, softening and soothing manner.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, do as we have said in our previous advice for a live birth; and if there is no power to do so, tear it apart piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, do as we have said in treating abscesses that come in marriage; and if bleeding comes out, it should be restrained with tight binding, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose womb had killed an infant, then consulted another physician about it, and the other revived the infant.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared in the buttock and swelled so much that it opened up and began to rot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and I thought about it for a long time, but could not stop the wound from bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I place strong plaster, and from it comes out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I wish to treat the wound, and break many bones as long as the woman is in a good position; and the woman survives for a long time in this state, and then after a little while, a piece of pus comes out; and I do not remember this chapter being used except when a master finds something strange that he knows how to treat.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marriage back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the screw press, with which one measures books; and at each turn, both heads of the two levers move.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The cornets should be more slender than the restrainer, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the rod should be wide, and the edges of the rods, and a half palms long; and between the two limbs there should be two joints of the same rod, which are to be fastened at both ends, half a palm long or slightly more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the patient for opening when turning the horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another shape, having a slimmer and lighter appearance, should be made from a rod of ebony or boxwood resembling pincers; and it should have two prongs, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the patient's mouth with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs spread apart, then place the two prongs side by side in the patient's mouth, and hold the base of the instrument beneath her thighs; then use your hand on the entire instrument, as you have done with the pincers equally, according to the quantity that you wish to open the woman's mouth, until the ball does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all covered and multiplied according to their resemblance; and when the surgeons have prepared them, he works more quickly, and higher for humans due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Never despise the instrument that you have not prepared, because their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold back her lochia (afterbirth), and then make her vomit with medicines, and hold your hands on her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, you take a spoon or cup, and put warm water or covered pot with herbs that can open the mouth of the patient (woman), such as rue, anise, chamomile, camphor, centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or boiled in water over fire; then put a cup or spoon from the pot, and the other end into the woman's mouth, and hold it until the vapors enter the patient; then make her vomit as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient jumps up quickly.   \n\nSi ung de ses membres est ostez, si com avons dit, se le pointe et fai grosse pele pour que il ne refreigne, et on met en la plaie ung cestui qu’il ne demurra pas; si li coupe la veine ou il demande, et aucune fois ne demeurez pas.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this cure and does not heal as commanded, tell the woman to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or musk-scented water from aloe, then put it on nature, and let it be seconded; and when she has found it, take and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the man does not resist extraction; but it must be moved gently to right and left, then pull; it will come out and will dislocate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 If the man's mouth is stretched out (dislocated), we have said the cure for cleaning and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not heal from everything that we have said, then make sure you do not pull it out; but it must be tied to the woman's thigh, then clisterize with tetraformulated ointment; if he will come back and heal, but even so, when she can, she will emit a bad odor from her stomach and head, and infect the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, fumigations suitable for this are necessary: no ancient has proven fumigation of dill and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it looks like glass resembling a dog's head, and put the delicate neck into nature, and widen the shoulders over the fire; and let there be fumigation above the coals, and the tainting until it is spoiled, and repeat another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation   (This line does not have a complete sentence in Old French and is likely an incomplete or fragmentary text)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born without a foundation pierced, instead it is stopped up with a fine stitch: therefore, when balancing, the stitch should be pierced at its proper place, and not with a sharp splinter; ensure that the lapse is not touched; then put damp linen in wine and oil, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will burst open again, place a splint of wood and leave it for many hours, and remove it when the child is seen to go into the bedrooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes comes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess; it is necessary to cover the affected area: if it is a wound, as we have said, with the lard of pig.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come below the foundation are nodules, and those that grow above the foundation escape from under it or in the space between two parts, if with one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it becomes inflamed, and moisture wakes blistering or fine boils, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by those who notice whether there is excretion or windiness when the patient passes excrement, and in some cases it jumps upwards.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that penetrate to the bladder and halfway up the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh and notch of the pelvis.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one knows the fistula at its foundation, but not persistently: and it is that you bite your finger or foundation, and bite a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula where there is no tortuousness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If it is tortuous, push a fine plaster of thin linen or horse hair until you feel the plaster or the hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no purulent discharge or wind or worm, as we have said: know that it does not perforate; hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends up to the bladder or the passage for urine, if it discharges urine and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated up to the knee joint, then the pus comes to the surface; if there is no tortuosity and the pain subsides, it is that it has healed of itself, and there is no need for medicine or ointment; and in these persisting fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish healers who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In one who is not paralyzed and not old, seeking health through the use of iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; then lift the legs up to the thighs, and incline the thighs towards the belly; afterwards place a tent of pitch or wood, if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels pain around the foundation (pelvis), then it is necessary that you place your finger there to see if the tent has pierced it; and if you feel a hole or flesh, then it is paralysis; do not touch it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One must be able to heal some, but it happens little; and the aid one does, if it is that one heats the cautery subtle according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and puts it all hot in the fistula, until it comes out from the base; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred fibers are burned, which resemble a feather of an eye; and then cure it with moistened tents in butter, until that char is gone, then cure it with ointment soothing and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If this can be healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise and if the fistula is entered but not pierced to its base, and between your finger and the fistula there is a thick cover of skin or leather, and you see the fistula under this covering with care; if the base of the fistula is struck, and pushed towards the fistula, and then the cautery after, until it reaches the end of the fistula; and the fistula will be released, and charred; then burn the fibers that resemble a feather of an eye, and no more remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the flesh is cut open by itself and there is no exit, cauterize it with fire or medicinal ointment.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery brings about two good things: burning of these attached sores, and the stopping of blood and removal of moisture; then it heals wounds wet with tents filled with butter or cooked oats, until the flesh boils in the butter; then heal the wound with strong hot salve for dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it will heal and not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes out to the full depth of the foundation and is separated from the body, push your finger or a probe into it and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and between it is the cloth or the silk or sores, which is about to be pierced, there should not be any fear but faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you strike deep down, or if you can, place tents and heal as before; do not go too far, so as not to cover the foundation that holds the tent, and let the abscess come out by itself with will; then heal it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering from above the foundation, either through a tent or any other instrument provided; then disinfect the pus-filled wound in the sore, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula away from the foundation part: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are formed in this way: and it is when you push the skin into the fistula, and it is where the tip protrudes beneath the outer layer of skin above; then take a pointed probe of this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	Then insert one thread twisted into two, and push the tent into the fistula to its full length (?) at the end of the thread.    --> Then insert one thread twisted together, and push the tent all the way into the fistula up to the end of the thread.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is perforated along the edge of the foundation within, then pull the thread from that opening so that you push your finger or foundation and draw out its head; bring together the two ends of the thread, squeeze them against each other, and leave for a day or two; hold them together as often as they pull apart, until the threads cut through the char that are between them and the pus is released; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.   Car il est doulent et grant peril por li laisser ouvir et non percier.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is not advisable to cover the wound while it is still gaping, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spur-shaped spina from which a fistula is made is very sharp at one end and blunt on the other; and yet, it should not be struck where it should not be struck, as you can see here.
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Abscesses are of two kinds: either they are within the foundation like a piece of resin, with small and large ones, and inside there is blood, and there is one or more, and they are displaced from their foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are displaced have little moisture, and at the same time or a little citron juice or blood, and have the color of flesh. The cure for these abscesses that are within the foundation is to command the patient to strain while in bed until the foundations subside, and the pus appears; if you hurry, bind it with tweezers or your nail, then strike its roots; and if the pus cannot be held because of the moisture, take a piece of linen or cotton or a piece of camel hair; wrap them around it and hold them with your fingers, then strike, and sprinkle some hot powders on top instead of cautery; or you can cauterize as described in the chapter on cautery, after which you treat other wounds until they are healed. If the foundations cannot be expelled, clisterize the patient with a bitter and sharp clisterum to wash what is around the foundation, so that it may come out openly; but if the patient resists, and if the pus has left the foundation, the cure is easy; you can grasp them with tweezers or tweezers, strike them, and treat as we have said, until they are healed, and fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you stitch the wound in this manner: take twisted thread, insert it into a needle, then pull the thread up and pierce the needle from the other side, turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, making it wide; tighten the thread, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving the excess blood to flow out; then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch on the wound foundation, and command the patient to rest; then let it be until it drains, and when it stops draining, treat it with ointment and other treatments until it heals.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The drying of fires or foundations
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often happens the drying of fires in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine has no effect.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you burn the bark of a willow twig or your fingernail with a hot iron so it does not get wet; then cure it until it heals as needed; and if it cannot heal, repeat the shaving more strongly than before, until it bleeds and is burnt; then cure it until it heals.
dou fremit	the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Formica (an insect) is a small growth found before the chest, and it grows very deep; sometimes it strikes the throat, and one feels it like death by shivering, and it spreads throughout the body, more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is that you take a reed of goose quill or a strong feather, and place the reed on the shivering, until it envelops it completely; then turn your hand along the entire length of the reed until it covers the shivering completely and drives it in deep, burning its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish to do so, make it like a catapult of tar or iron in this form, and let it be subtle within and traverse above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, for fear of causing pain, and press gently; And if you wish to cauterize the trembling (of a wound), as is explained in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster (enema)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make an enema of silver or arsenic, or melted tar or honey; and sometimes they make small and large instruments according to the ones brought in.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when treating children who are weak and suffering, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cluster is both small and large; it should be placed over a wide area where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it should have an opening where the abdomen is joined, as you see, and the chest should be pierced within; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other one; and fill the abdomen with medicine from a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce it all around with small holes; and between each hole there should be some space, then insert strong thread through each hole crosswise, and close the abdomen like a bag; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to an instrument with a strong thread, then bandage; and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the bandage with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the ministers should examine it with both hands until it is completely visible, then remove the bandage, and make the patient lie down on his back, and if the medicine appears to come out, hold it as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it will be a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plaster him in case of intestinal disease and the medicine hastens to heal, continue to apply it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are ulcerated or abscessed, whether they are soft like in children, then use a subtle enema; and this is the form of the subtle enema when the skin is stretched:
des plaies	for wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds; now I will tell you about the care of hands and medicines, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to how they were made, and according to the places where the wounds were made, and because of what they were caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things that wounds are made from are by hitting with a stone, cutting with a sword or knife, lance or mace or similar things; or whatever is made according to the body parts, such as wounds on the neck, head, thigh, belly, liver and similar limbs; I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will start with simple wounds of the head, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or an injury comes, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to arrow puncture or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large; raise doubt about abscess formation: if there is pus from the wound, make it heal immediately from the head itself, even if blood comes from the wound; let the patient empty himself of excessive wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it does not want to heal, reduce his food intake, do not drink wine, and do not eat meat or char; place on the wound if pus comes from it, a slightly dampened woolen cloth in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; if there is no pus, place on the fresh wound that has not moved by the air, a powder (that I will say a little later); and if the fire has moved it, place some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is large like a sword's size and the lips cannot be brought together by force, bring them together by stitching, as I shall explain in abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, pierced and does not stay in place, press it; then cure the wound with medicine, put hard fat instead of skin, and command the patient to eat thick foods such as cooked heads (testes) and wheat, also like peas, etc.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if the skin or flesh becomes rotten and is not attached to the bone, press it all out and throw away the pus, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by medicine, squeeze it (the affected area), and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: and it is that you put this powder which hardens as soon as the arrows have moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and grind the mixture finely, then apply it to the wound and press it firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it unbandaged if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with only charcoal when there is no incense or the blood of a dragon, but the wound has not healed over yet.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the fire has burned the wound, especially in that case, do not put this powder on it; instead, apply some digestible ointments or barley flour poultice made with water and honey, until it turns green; then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if a bone breakage comes with the wound, and it is small, draw it out with fine forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If there is a wound in the neck and it is simple (uncomplicated), there is no difference between this and one in the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is a nerve, there should be no other device but to let it heal naturally, and not put anything restraining, for it hurts the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body; but let the medicine be warm, such as warm water washed in sweet oil, and boiled water also washed in this way, and other stones of the same kind, according to this manner, and immediately moist.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then wrap it with strips of linen until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and inflamed and full of pus, pierce it or lower it; if the arteries are cut, bleeding follows, so cauterize, lance, and cauterize as needed; if the spine in the throat is cut, or the trachea, and the windpipe is guarded, so that the meat goes upward to the throat and does not touch the throat but is replaced according to its natural shape; then press gently, and leave it for several days, then treat with rejected ointments until it heals; if the wound presses on the bone, cut it; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out as you can, and leave those that you cannot have, until the wound discharges and is drained and aligned; if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder over it, as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, check if there are any signs of pus coming from the wound: then you know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep and is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder immediately nor bind it for the blood that prevents coagulation, and let it return to the heart, and leave the patient; but apply attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound for drawing out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 or 4 days, or more; no spasm, bad tremor of heart or other signs of pus will come; and when you see good conditions, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the wound and other treatments as long as it is healthy; if it cannot heal, then open it immediately, since there is a fistula; cure it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, large, or in the back, then treat what is in front of it; if it is large, stitch it; if it is small, use powder; and if it is pressed against the bone and has pieces, either clean the wound and pull out any loose parts; but if they are not loose, let the wound drain until it heals naturally. The judgement for other wounds on different body parts is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	the dislocation of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	1. The dismemberment of the abdomen is great, medium, and small; from a large wound, the intestines sometimes protrude once, or the edges of the intestines, making insertion difficult; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because it is harder to put the intestines back in place if not done carefully; as they inflate suddenly when they feel cold, and this makes it harder for them to go back in, and therefore a medium-sized wound is better, because the intestines can be manipulated more easily back into their place than with other wounds. And know that the incision of the abdomen is according to four methods: the two common sutures occur in the abdominal suture, and the sutures of the other body parts and the other specific ones are common for the other wounds; but they are more appropriate with the abdominal suture, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes from it, it is easy to treat, as there are two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, heat it in one of these ways: either moisten a sponge or dampen a cloth only in warm water, or you cook in hot wine and cinnamon and juniper and thorns, and hold the intestines until the swelling disappears; and sometimes do this with restraining wine, and it should be allowed to cool to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling spread, moisten the intestine with warm or hot water and bitter herbs, for thus the entrance is opened a little; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to remove hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to be allowed to cool before cutting, but we should not cut too much without necessity; and this is the tool for splitting: pierce inside the hump and spread outward, and look at this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is widened and the intestines fall out, put them back in place according to their natural form in their proper position, if you have the power to do so, for it is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part below the stomach, you must make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the stomach, then you should raise the head and the feet more than the parts below, and similarly, when the rupture of the stomach is in one of the two sides, you must focus on ensuring that the damaged side is higher than the other; and in this way, you should attend to both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 Small wounds, place what is necessary for you, then take a compassionate person with a hand to treat the wound, and bring the lips together; this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or more than one, depending on the width of the wound, then leave a gap at the edge of the wound and insert a needle where there is strong thread; pierce the two layers of skin with the two layers of tendon, which is under the skin, from that side to the other, until you have made a hole through it, and bring together the three edges; then tie a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound accordingly, then leave a gap and insert another needle; tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue this way according to your needs for needles, until the entire wound is held together; let the needles be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because very fine needles pierce through all the flesh and too thick ones cannot enter well: this is why they should be medium-sized. And do not insert the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, so as not to pierce and open the wound before it heals; then clip the needle heads, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place weights or bandages on the needle heads to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound heals. This method of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because a single needle or two can perform a second stitch if necessary, and it is that you bring together the layers of skin and tendon with one needle where there is strong thread; and when you have pierced all four sides, remove the needle to the part where you began, in the way cloth is sewn; leave space between each stitch the thickness of a minor eggshell. This stitching method is called suturing by men, and I sewed a wound with it on a man who had a belly wound caused by a knife, which was more than one palm wide, and the intestines were about two palms deep inside, and the wound was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestine when it had been twenty-four hours, and the wound healed for fifteen days, and it was cured, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 They had judged him that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal it with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed cotton old twice a day on the wound, and washed it with water of honey until it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pierce from the outer part to inside straight; when it has pierced the skin right through, place the tip or stitch of the needle where you put in the needle, and pierce it again from the inner part outwards to the outer; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew as a skinner does fur, and leave one side open, then take up the other side until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of stitching, as Galen calls it, is when two parts are brought together naturally, and one end of the skin is applied to the other end, in this way: insert a needle or the point of the mirror, and pierce only that place; leave the two ends of the skin; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner, through the two ends of the skin; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner, in the two other holes that are opposite each other on the other side; and this is the moving manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens uses this phrase and it is borne out by all witnesses, that the abdomen should be sewn with two needles, each with thread; one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew bags; and know that when the wound is within the abdomen, the stitching is more difficult than elsewhere on the abdomen.
