Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgement of the wound is similar to that of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound with all its blood, after the arrows have moved it, then you restore the intestine and the purse; afterwards put powder strengthening flesh on it, and if the arrow has moved it, then put any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew up the flesh, and bind the sifac, and apply the mirach; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then immediately put old cotton on it, and turn it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You need no other medicine for many conditions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may infect the main members, then moisten thin linen in warm oil or rose oil, and put it around the injuries, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling, and this often occurs, then clisterize with black wine, especially when the swelling comes up to the intestines; and pierce it through, and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is because of the swellings in the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the gristle (sinew) leaps from the wound, reset it in place as an intestine does while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned black, you must cut away the black part where blood does not come out, because there are veins and arteries there; then take hold of what is between the ligaments, and hang the two heads (of the bones) hanging from the part below the wound towards outside to facilitate the extraction when the gristle leaps, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the boil rupture
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen a man pierced or wounded by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there were emissions and windings; I treated it according to what I knew, and did not stop subliming until it healed, and the ligaments adhered.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I see it sutured, I doubted that the patient had trouble in his stomach; and there was no problem, but he improved in better condition, and ate and drank; and any experienced person said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied up in such a way: take strong farts, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the fart has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips, so that it stretches its mouth open; and then strike the head, and hold it so that it cannot undo itself, then put another fart after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head of the intestine becomes inflamed, it causes no harm to the patient, and the intestine can be tied with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, as follows: take the end of this intestinal thread that is sharpened, then tie it to the head of a linen thread twisted in a similar manner, then insert the thread into the needle, sew the intestine, and draw the stitches along the wound; and this method of suturing is not harmful except by faith and hope. If the injury is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the greater intestines, there is no trick or healthiness, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or...
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it heals and forms a swelling, is universally called "fistula," and likewise when it bursts and empties.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And fistula is, according to the truth, a hard and white nodule, where there is no pain felt, and it swells like the feather of a bird; sometimes it clears up with a clear discharge, and at other times it becomes thick; sometimes it is small, and at other times it is quite large; I have spoken about it in the section on wounds, that every wound that is not healed and has no flesh, is not healed except by one of the nine causes: that is to say, due to the small amount of blood or body fluid; or because of its bad quality; or because there is hard matter within, under the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much discharge; or the wound is deep, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because corruption is a form of pestilence; or because the digestion in that region is slow, and healing is slow and weak, and it recedes naturally; or there are veins or bones: I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the medicines for treatment in the section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall tell you the cure for a fistula made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all the members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or at the anus, or intestines, or bladder, or one of the ribs, or the spine on the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it occurs in the principle member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance for them; and if any fistula does not come up to the level I have said, and you have confidence in its cure, and you observe it, take a tent of wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, use it; and if the fistula is twisted, look for a fine tent of yarn, because yarn bends with twists; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot find it with tents, cauterize it through one of the holes, because moisture goes from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then clean it as well as you can, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is filled up, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and where it is; and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foreign matter and corrupt charcoal inside; and then cure it until it heals, and if the fistula is well penetrated from a straight direction, then cut through it entirely, as much as you can, then put wet tents soaked in medicine on it, and push them up to the end of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess matter that remains inside; and then put ointments made with healthy charcoal on it, until it heals; and if it does not heal by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If neither vein nor artery presses or major limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all corruption is removed, then treat with charms as necessary until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, drain pus as before, know that you are not yet at the fountain: expose and scrape as deep as possible, remove all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it; and if there is only a little corrupted bone, and you can extract it with pliers, remove it with the appropriate tool for this purpose, and if there are many bones, remove all of them, do not leave any; and if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, strike and subdue moisture and char, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove [the affected part] within an hour, put on the wound something stimulating decay, and leave it until the flesh surrounds the bones, and then the bones will be removed more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of a leg or thigh, press the corruption only until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part corrupted, and comes to the marrow of the bone; it must be excised and covered up to the corruption, and then cured until it heals; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so you can take an example and help with your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something inside his body that caused matter to come to the leg, and he had a large abscess, and there was no cause for it to open; but they mistakenly opened the abscesses many times due to their folly, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and much moisture came from the body; and many people tried to cure him for two years, and there was no skilled hand among them until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they were using, and what flowed out through the sores at great intervals; and the young man's body became red, and he had a citrus-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I stitched a tent in one of the wounds, and then searched all the wounds, and found that some were coming together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I then hurried and cut in one of the wounds as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot came to the bone within; what appeared to me was the rotten bone, and I thought there was no other corruption except that which I left; and for a long time I began to treat the wound with medicinal salves, but could not heal it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the rot continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then left it, and intended to set the bone; but I could not do so more than I cut around a palm of the bone, and exposed it completely to the air, then set it with medicines; and it healed quickly and was soon mended, and no further work needed to be done except due to the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and out of fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the blood evacuation, it often heals entirely, and a hard cyst grows in the place of the bone, and it has a good disposition and no harm or contrary effect at all, neither at the side nor at coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated like this: take a thread, and tie it to the end of the open bone, and command someone to stretch it up; then place another larger thread on top of the cyst that is under the bone, and tie it so that you pull out the corrupt cyst from below, and uncover the cyst in the place where you want to be, so that it does not irritate the cyst; place a splint or a stick underneath the bone to cover the corrupt cyst; and it must be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and it must be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, cover the flesh entirely; then place fire underneath, and then be from one part to another the corruption, and let the iron [or instrument for correction] be along the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, strike the corrupted joint, and be the bone or it on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other opening but to cover [it]; and if the corruption is at the tip of the hand or foot, it is a very difficult thing, but still you must investigate the corruption, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not harm the vein or the nerve; and know that the cutting tool and the iron for covering bones are many, according to the type of bone and the appearance of the wound, and its thickness and subtlety, and its size and smallness, and hardness; and therefore it is necessary to adapt the instrument to each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the understanding of this art, and the testimony of the characteristics of diseases; thus consider the tool you need according to what it should be.
dou feu	hot fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may rot internally or externally; and when you have medicine to cure the corruption of that member, but it does not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death by this or by a greater evil, which is the loss of the limb; and the signs are that the limbs turn black as if burned by fire, and afterward they become darker, because the corruption spreads from one member to another and takes over the whole body; hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of certain venomous animals like sea scorpion and viper and similar, cover the head of the affected limb and do not give them room to reach up to your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes up to the hand, strike at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, strike at the side; and if it passes the side, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus do as when the corrosion comes or falls: if it comes at the first joint, then strike after the next joint; and if it comes or falls, strike the entire bone; and if it goes into the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means of help for the patient but to let him die; and the method of striking or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister on the lower ligament, and another minister on the upper ligament, and you cut the flesh between the two ligaments with a thin spatula, until the bone is exposed; then strike or sew, and place a piece of linen cloth on each side so that the sewing does not touch the healthy part, and cause the patient further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. And when blood flow occurs while you operate, cauterize the area immediately, or apply certain powders that restrict bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the limb with a suitable bandage and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my town: he had a black spot that looked like a burn by fire, and that corrosion first appeared on his foot, consuming all of the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he cut off the foot, and it healed; and a long time later the corrosion returned to his hand or fingers, and it came to me, and I applied reactive substances after purification of the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he asked that I amputate his hand, but I refused because I had hope of healing the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the vitality of man was weak; and he lost all hope, returned to his earth, and cut off his own hand, and it healed; and I have not heard this story except because such things are done when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess appears in a charred place and remains so long that it forms a large swelling; and then it becomes red and pierces through, and the swelling jumps out, leaving the place open as a wound does, just like a vassal's; and the skin that is on top is as thin as fine linen, and it will not penetrate to the bone or the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", not "fistule"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone completely, it is called "fistule"; and the skin should be cut all around, just like one cuts fine linen; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. And if the skin hardens [and] corruption is not complete, and the skin is swollen with pus, treat it thus: look to see if the breasts are large and the boil that is within them is full of foul smell, then clisterize with Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take asafetida, oil, pitch, equally, and cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; and then take according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and clisterize the breast, and press out the pus; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it while straining; do this often, until the breast is cleansed and the pus is gone; and at times clisterize with water of ashes, when the Egyptian medicine is not present, and take ashes from a vine stick, pour water over it, then strain it, and clisterize until you know that the breast is clean; and if the patient cannot endure it, or the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then clisterize with water and honey or mead, where the honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the pus harden; when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is cleaned, then clisterize with whatever makes it produce charcoal in it, and take emplastrum definitive, and mix it with oil of roses and vinegar; or clisterize with various medicines and ointments, of which I have told the properties or the treatment of the ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the clistering stick cannot enter it, then enlarge it slightly with a knife, and apply an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, so that it can be opened; and if the wound is too large, make it smaller, but only enough for the hand or clistering stick to enter, and if the boil is above, press down on it or press lower.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the bowels are fully dilated, do not let anything enter char; and if you cannot cover the belly with cloth as you see, arrange it in such a way that the bowels move downwards as much as possible, for when the bowels are fully dilated, do not let anything enter char and if you cannot cover the belly with cloth as you see, arrange it in this manner: the bowels move lightly downwards, and do not leave anything of the bowel; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place them on a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then press firmly towards the wound opening which is wider than the first, then apply ointment gently on the other cloth according to the size of the wound opening, and place it on the wound opening to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days once; and the one who is on the wound opening removes it often to dislocate the bowel, and knows what comes from the bowel, whether it is poison or pus or gas or undigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see the nature that rises on the wound opening, know that the bowels have healed and are approaching health; then release it in the morning or the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts swell improperly after many days, know that the breasts do not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisonous worms attack after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For those who delay healing of flesh in their wounds, and for those who do the opposite; and if they consume food indigestibly after many days, know that the breast will not heal; and if the breast is slow to heal, and has become swollen, apply drying medicines with dry substance and wet virtue, such as linseed oil, because it contains a great part of vitriol, which is the last resort; use linseed oil, mix it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine as its substance; then cook it and use it; and if linseed oil is not present, take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them, powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; then spread the plaster on the breast, and sometimes administer an astrologer's long root, which is also like flour and centaur; and use simple or compound herbs: grind them, make a powder, and put it on the honey I have said, and use it; and if the wound is deep and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has spread throughout, and makes an impression in the bone or hard parts or ligaments; treat with fistula cure as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or toe, or by chance arises in other places; and when it swells and care is not taken, if the abscess grows, it runs and spreads until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it may grow entirely; and the corrosion comes up to the bone, causing pain that smells bad, and the joints become wide, and the color becomes putrid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, then you must cut off all the excess that remains from the nail, followed by cauterizing the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cauteries are very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail grows into the flesh, starts to swell, and bleed, it is necessary that you place the heated iron beneath the nail so as not to burn the skin, push up the nail slightly, strike gently and lightly on the root of the nail, and apply hot and corrosive medicines above it in order to remove all; then let it heal until it is sound.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 If the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw it out, because as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; if you see that it needs to be corroded, do so as before said, then let it heal until it is sound; and if it is wounded and painful, you must first make it healthy; then cut the nail with a sharp chisel diagonally above, but watch that the cutting does not reach the skin beneath the nail because the patient would feel too much pain; if this happens, place something to relieve it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One should cauterize the tumor that arises in some people's hands accidentally, and sometimes it has flesh or bone, or even a nail; and one of them is born on the root of the joint or in any of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The tumor that arises in the finger does not move, but the one that arises at the joint of the finger may move; the size of the fleshly tumor is small, in this manner: cut it off at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; cover it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For the tumor that arises or should be in the last finger, it is necessary to first cut off the round flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate cautery, and treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Fractures come together in the joints due to birth, injury, burns, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If you have to cauter that sore, it should heal according to its natural shapes; then put between two tent or cloths moistened in rose oil so they do not stick; or you put between two pieces of subtle plank until the wound is healed as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of his hands comes with the palm towards the joint, you strike that joint as needed.
des vils	 of villains (in this context, "villain" is a term used to refer to common people or peasants)
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 These are the large veins swollen with excessive melancholic fluid that appear in various parts of the body; and it happens more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purges of bile on occasion, and then heal with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is according to two ways: one is that you cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you tie up the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The size of the incision is as follows: first, heat the leg with very hot water, until the flesh becomes soft, then hold the patient's leg from above the calf to the part below the kneecap; then make a large cut in the vein, either at I or II or III, and remove black blood up to your hand, as much blood as the strength of the patient can endure; then tie it, and order him to bind with food that turns the urine dark; start the evacuation and healing again when the veins are full, and this helps the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dressing of the wound is as follows: if there is much hair on the patient's leg, shave it, then place him in water or heat his leg with fire and apply hot water, until the flesh turns red and the veins swell; if you don't have water, heat the leg with fire. Then make an incision along the long side of the thigh towards the knee or below the calf; open the skin around the vein on both sides, revealing it as soon as it is felt; it will appear red and black, and when it appears, it looks like a white cord; then push the fat down, allowing it to swell under the skin, and then lightly close the incision, then make another incision at a different place, 3 inches away from the first one or more if necessary; then open the skin over the vein again, revealing it as before, then remove the blood, as you have done before, and repeat the incision at another spot, as you did before; then make another cut, or multiple cuts if needed, until all the blood is removed, then close it; if you cannot remove or lift the blood, insert a thick double-threaded needle into it and pull it, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; be careful not to let it burst, as it cannot be drawn or lifted if it does, and this harms the patient; when you have treated it all, place linen dampened in wine and oil on the wound, and nurse it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, you should cut it open forcefully, but do not cover it up; pull it out as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to strike the face is curved, but it does not cut through; instead it should be used to open a vein. It is thick and large because if it were thin, it would pierce the skin, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein (or artery)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is located in the legs, in hot areas where no grass or trees grow, and on dry ground; it may also occur elsewhere, but this happens due to a worm that arises from under the skin, as it comes within the body like a serpent and penetrates between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the joint changes and the vein begins to forcefully issue forth, just as the root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the joint opens, you must cover it with a piece of wood about 7 to 12 inches long, and sew it, and leave the wood on the leg, and each time it starts to swell out, you should re-cover it with the wood and sew it; if it is too long, cut off part of it and cover the remaining, and do not sew near its root, as long as it is completely issued; for if you sew it, it returns into the flesh, bringing abscess and pus or poison and a bad disease. Therefore, it must be treated little by little until it reaches the neck, and nothing remains in the body. Sometimes this vein, when it is treated, can reach 5 or 10 inches long, and once I had a man who had one that was 10 inches long. When you cut it open, push a plaster or a plug into it, and pierce it all the way through, so that everything comes out of it. The matter inside should be emptied, and medicines for pus should be applied to it daily, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And at times this vein is opened wide, especially when it gapes in the joint of the foot or hand, and much bleeding ensues, causing it to spurt; then heal it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 from worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "beef disease," because it often occurs with cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body expanding and contracting, and one can feel it move from member to member until it reaches the skin or leaves, and jumps away; and it causes intestinal poisoning of certain humors, such as worms, serpents, larvae, or roundworms in the stomach; and doubt is cast on its malice, for when it travels through the body, and it rises to the head, and reaches the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to be treated and drawn, one cannot force it but when it goes; therefore, you must first tie the limb above and below with a strong ligament tightly, then strike it and draw it out, and if its head enters fully into the flesh, and you do not feel it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it burns oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold under it a bellows shaped cork, then strike it and draw it out; and you must use the patient with purifying of the body medicines soluble for bad humors, and prevent him from eating sour foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 The pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land and it is a pain that moves from one member to another; and I have seen this as I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman and found her arm swollen, and shortly after saw a small boil in the armpit; then I felt it rise like a worm towards the shoulder much more quickly than anything else, just as silver cuts one thing from another; the pain departed from that place and pierced the shoulder, then a little later ran throughout the body, so she came to the other arm; then she said that it returned around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 In addition, I wanted many who were suffering pain to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in a woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins open, and because of this appeared that constrained windiness; and they do not understand according to this reason those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you wish to cure this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, press it both above and below quickly, then strike on it so that the constrained windiness goes from the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your eyes, cure it with those who expel windiness, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their shapes and according to the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of them [arrows] is that there are some with large points and small, smooth and solid; and some with two tips, and those with tongues, and those with spikes; and the one that falls in any member falls according to two ways: either in a principal member, like brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls in any part of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears: if it is necessary to extract this arrow, for death comes in many ways after; and when this ill sign does not appear at all, and the arrow is not fully embedded, pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces it, and the swelling that is on top of the brain, is similar to scotomia (loss of vision), sagitta (arrow wound), esverted eye, reddening in the eyes, inflammation and redness of tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes without swelling in the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it may lose speech and voice; and it jumps from a wound with white moisture resembling pus, and also as boiling of char; and if this sign appears to you, refrain from treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it had been thrust into a hard object, not empty; and perhaps the arrow swells like a pustule, with black blood coming out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore there should be no doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow that has pierced the flesh is without bubbles jumping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and seeks for the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the bed of hay, it is buried in the ribs; and it emits a great groan and great pain and breaths heavily; and all the members of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or food remains stuck in the wound, by chance anything from undigested meat may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach, and something from the undigested intestines jumps out of the wound, there is no hope for the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes the bladder and urine jumps out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members such as the face and neck, shoulder and back, chest and arms, spine of the back, pelvis and legs, and similar limbs are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason you should do something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow fell or pierced into the root of his nose: I pulled it out from another side under the fat of the ear, and it was found senseless.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And pulled out an arrow that fell into the grease of the oil under the paper, and the arrow was curved, and could not be reached but the tip towards the foot, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all iron-headed ears; the player was senseless, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pulled out an Arabic arrow from a Christian's throat, and the arrow had iron ears; I sharpened the points, and carefully pulled it out, and the Christian was senseless.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And he drew an arrow from the man who was struck or wounded, and thought that he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his position did not change at all; I cut above the arrow, and made it come out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you want to treat a man who has an arrow lodged in his chest or back, and the wound is closed over it; if the arrow remains inside him without moving his natural positions, and no harm is found in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And you want to treat another man who has an arrow in his face, and the wound is closed over it; and he suffers great pain for a long time; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And draw out an arrow from the body of the prince, the king who was struck in the neck, and he was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was entirely lodged. I was called to the treatment after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I probed it with a thin probe and did not feel anything; but he felt sharpness and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I placed a plaster attractive and digestive on the spot because the wound did not swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I kept the plaster on for many days, and healed the wound directly, and the patient remained for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his neck; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I put the wound medicine corrosive on for many days until it opened, and then I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which stuck in place; next, I cauterized the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow became visible; and the wound healed well within four months, and then it broke open again where I had nailed the pliers, and the flesh on either side could not close; therefore, I did not stop refining and devising ways to extract the arrows, until I made the pliers properly fitted for this purpose, as will be described at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the mirrors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I will restore it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, but I do not say all of it, for books cannot entirely grasp it; but wise masters understand well a little thing and concerning that which is present and failing, they discover nine works, and new tools, in the diminishment of foreign things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not pierce the members where they are inserted except in two ways: either by the side through which they enter, or from another part; and that which springs forth through the side where it enters is an arrow entering into the fleshy parts, and sometimes springs out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, leave it until the flesh is torn around, and align the joint; and in the same way, if it is pierced into the bone and cannot come out, leave it for a few days and move it every day; then it will jump, and if it does not jump, pierce all around with a very sharp instrument, until the muscles around are loosened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If the arrow is pierced into the head's bone and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the incidents I mentioned earlier occur: do not pull it out at all, but let it remain evenly for a few days, because if the arrow reaches such a place, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not embedded beyond the bone only and does not reach deeply, and the patient remains ill for some days with bad accidents, then you should try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted, administer a plaster around it, as I told you earlier; then heal the wound when it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is embedded deep within the body and cannot be seen, you should search for it thoroughly; if you feel it, draw it out with any suitable tool; if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, make an incision as large as necessary; draw the arrow and break off the ears on it if there are any, then grind away the part of the shaft that is embedded in the flesh as much as you can, then bend or break the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow when pulling it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, press the arrowhead against the bones around it, then pull it out, as extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood obstructs [the procedure], bring to mind what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve or vein, and use a device as you can safely draw out the arrowhead, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot do so, position him according to what the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrowhead coming from elsewhere, if it penetrates anything, or the skin is inflamed around it as one can see or sense clearly; cut through it then, until the pincers can grasp it, and then pull it out; if it pops out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round as much as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still and then continue the extraction as long as it comes forth; and if it is of an arrow, push it all in; and if it is broken, you should administer grease to make it slippery, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push harder, and when the arrow is slipped in, push the instrument in pointedly for easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, as you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls into the chest or abdomen or bladder or side and is close, and you can cover it, do so; but beware of covering the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and sew up the wound if needed, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the growing hair at its tip is like a bird's feather, to guide the arrowhead. [Here, "li forme dou boutant cheveit" can be understood as "the shape of growing hair tips", and "com li penne d’un oisel" means "like a bird's feather".]
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps (tongue-like instrument) for insertion and removal is as follows:
