des voinnes dou cors communes	openings of the body's common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 From the veins from which one recovers are thirty-one, of which the head is sixteen, namely: two veins that are after the ears, called "the two 'herbech'"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples visible; and the two veins that are in the two eyes, called "aspirers"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two veins that are at the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed are five in each arm: one is called the cephalic, and it is situated on the left side of the chest and the common people call it "vein of the head"; the middle one is called "fistula", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic vein is on the right side of the chest and the common people call it "ventricle vein", and it is above the elbow, and it is the one that opens manifestly near the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The cubital is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and there are two of them; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the wrist of the left side of the chest, and the second saphenous which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nesse" that is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The first hairs of the arteries located behind the ears assist with old-time catharsis and emigration; and the nature of these hairs, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head, and scrub the place where the arteries are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw so that both arteries appear behind the ears on their dependent places from the head; hold them there until you feel the pulse beneath your hand; then take the lancet, and push it through the artery up to the bone, then pull your whole hand along the entire artery, piercing and the skin and the artery well two times through; and make blood flow until you see; then tie and hold it until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first artery in the two temples is useful to migraine, sciatica, and optometry which are common ailments, and to cure eye pain; the quality of the artery is as I have said: when the patient turns his neck so that both veins appear openly; you feel a pulsation beneath your thumb, then apply pressure on it; raise the incision above your thumbnail towards your index finger, insert the lancet, raise the vein, and cut it, as you have done in other veins, and collect blood according to your need; then release the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; form a bandage and leave it until it is healed; we have spoken about its treatment and extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for old facial diseases that have migrated and reddened; and their qualities are such that the patient turns his neck while twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Place the point on the vein and press with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to its quantity that you see; then release the neck of the patient, and tie the vein until it is healed and never perform this operation with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Furthermore, the flames should not be too sharp, and it is better to proceed obliquely because the bone is close, and there is danger of breaking the flame when it is narrow.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The vein of the two eyes located in the tear ducts helps in the treatment of inflammation, redness, swelling, and facial diseases; their qualities are such that the patient turns his neck while twisting with any restraint, as previously mentioned; then heal it, and make the incision through the vein a short distance from the flame but wide enough, for there is no pain.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then make a tourniquet of blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The following of the vein in the nose is beneficial for ague, scrofula, and sicknesses of the face, such as migraines and redness that come from the face, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the vein are that the patient stretches his neck, then his nose to your left hand, takes subtle flame long, and pierces it between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well in whom, and the wound will begin to heal soon; do not go too deep, and make the bleeding stop according to your necessity, then let it rest for a night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The saline of the two tendons helps in the straightening of the ankle, at the beginning of swelling, and in many diseases, and pus formation, and corrosion, and herpes, and abscesses; and the qualities of the saline are such that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and if the master is standing above the patient's head, and the patient lies on the chair, then open the vein along its length slightly widely, then draw the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do the same in another vein, then untie the ligament, and gently tighten all the veins so that the patient does not strain; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the healing of the shoulders
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The saliva from the veins of the lips above helps to clot in the mouth and contributes to the corruption of gums, fissures in lips, and tooth and surrounding issues.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of healing are to make the patient sit before you, hold their neck as I have said; then turn the shoulder, and look at both veins, one is on the right shoulder and the other on the left, and they can be recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the small veins around them: strike one and the other, and if you do not know which one it is, or if you are in doubt, strike the largest of each pair, and do the same for the upper and lower ones, as it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The healing of the veins beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic healing, and it is in the straining of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of healing are that the patient should sit between your hands before the sun, lift the tongue, and look beneath on each side for a black vein: heal one and the other, but do not go too deep, as below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins from which one commonly heals are healed according to two methods: either by pricking with a lance that burns widely, or with olive oil fine as you know it, and is called "anesil"; and they are large and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrhine is very famous, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 It is necessary to open hairless veins that contain thick blood and are troubled; this is the form of oil-burning.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more precisely, and is for thinning the subtle veins where there is fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, neck, chest, and belly; it is necessary for the patient to heal completely, and he must be cauterized from the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 If the artery is touched and bleeding occurs, it should be stopped as I have said; but the flame should not be pricked, but rather cut like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 If the basilica does not open clearly, you should force it to open and change another one, or seek any other opening in its place, such as the vein at the elbow; it opens clearly; and when touching the flame, use a lancet as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 If you want to find the location of the vein, you must also extend the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot for making the incision, bind the arm tightly, and burn the vein with a lancet; be careful not to wound the artery when you see the vein inflated because it is an artery - avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rise high as a child's urine, and the patient is red and subtle, know that this is not from an artery: hurry then, and place your finger long on it, then remove your finger when the patient does not bleed anymore; leave the arm in this state, and do not move it by the patient; be afraid, and do not move it until it becomes healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not cauterized and it starts to bleed, and there is no medicine present, then seize the artery if it opens up, as it can be stopped by compressing it; stop the bleeding of the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fustic bark, cut it and take one half and lay it on top until the next day; if it does not bleed, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow; but the stopping of the bleeding should not be overdone in many ways due to the smallness of the wound and the tension of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The first vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins as we have said; therefore, the master must press for the nerve that is below, and if it bleeds too much when pierced and he finds the nerve, it swells and the patient feels pain and may not heal; and this nerve opens up often, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must cauterize it with the instrument; pull away the nerve as far as your strength allows.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make an incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The first vein of the head helps to drain blood from the head and the eyes; it needs to be cauterized by olive oil or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Moreover, it is necessary to seek the lighter joint, and not to worry if it needs to be done the first time, and you may start again; and sometimes the joints swell in some people, when it should be done for the first time, but do not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not performed unless to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and it should be done in one of the three veins: cephalic, femoral, or basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first day or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The healing administered for diseases has no set hour determined, but when there is need of day or night, at all hours and in every tense; and it is not appropriate to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor women bearing fruit except during the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	The patient who have passed sixty years, should not heal themselves.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when anyone wishes to be healed, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that their intestines are cleansed with a gentle enema, if they have retained much wind, so that the veins do not carry excess waste to the main organs; nor should one heal him who is excessively salted with food, or drunk, until he is sober, nor those who are dropsical; and if healing is done after a colonic affliction, vomiting, abdominal disorder, multiple urination at women, and labor, watchfulness, and fasting, and those suffering from poison or injury to the body; then refine the humors, if he is not fat, by food and drink and medicines, if you have the power; then immerse in water, unless anything prevents it, to thin the blood, and heal from the vein on the side of the third finger, as we have said; and keep him on that day from labor, pain, lust, and similar things; and be cheerful and joyful, and let the healer be higher than the one being healed, and rub his arm two or three times, then gently pull out the thread above, for when it is too tight or thin, it cannot heal without; then rub the site with the hand until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's fingers with a spoonful of old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand under that vein below the site where you wish to heal, so that the vein does not flee and fail when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 There are veins that resemble cords in a sieve, and there are some that are filled with pus, so that when you put the fire on them, they shrink from the flame and cannot open the vein, and it is thus with these; if the vein is opened, the wound is too narrow, therefore the sewer must be aware of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it's good; but if not, start again a little below or above that place where it is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the limb swells and the patient fears, let it rest for a day or two and do not tie the arm; perhaps there will come pus; do not enter the bath, then resume the sewer if he wishes; and if the wound is small or narrow, open it gently with a subtle knife and doubt if it does not appear that there will be much blood; firmly apply the fire to the wound itself immediately; and open it a little hastily, so that the limb swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not start draining it immediately, but put a little bit of oil on it, for it lightens the body with blood and is turned into this liquid by the oil; and administer the oil in every drainage when you drain the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this also works for scabs and boils, when it is placed on the place; if it becomes too thick, it dissolves and separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens when the opening of the vein is small, hasten, and put on the place a wet sponge in hot vinegar and oil, and press it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it remains in its place after several days without turning black or green, it will not hurt; and if you see, apply anything of aloes or myrrh, mixed with cumin, camphor, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance occur in the church's sanctuary: place your hand on it then, and if you find it soft under the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then do not place anything above what has been said, for in court without the artery; but make one dry plaster to harden it, then treat with other treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the amount of its power and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it large, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for one who is wounded and hollowed out, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it must be drained little by little, and it should be drained obliquely, not punctured; and this method of draining is safe from the displacement of blood and the compression of nerves, and it is more effective than draining long rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the body that requires draining, it is necessary to give soft bread soaked in grape juice; if it is scalded, drain blood three or four times. And for one of cold complexion, fast before draining with soft bread in syrup mixed, or syrup of aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and a pleasant-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if it hurts at the incision after a large flow of blood, then it is required that you apply crushed charcoal, fragrant subtle syrup, and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter of bleeding, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If one wants to burst open his arm or bleed elsewhere when weakened by repeated bleeding, it should be done little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If one wishes to burst open his arm after the first bleeding and has a strong heart, he should wait 6 hours following the first bleeding or the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If one wishes to bleed elsewhere, it should be done on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood within the body which is already heated and causes fever; it is necessary to draw out a large amount, and to open the incision as wide as possible until it stops bleeding; then you must follow all the conditions of the incision, and place your hand on top of the pulses when it stops bleeding, so that death does not come in its place, and this happens many times when the lancer is negligent; and it is not necessary to dislocate the arm and draw blood a second time, and the incision is closed, but you press firmly; nor if it is curved, extend the arm quickly, because that would be bad; rather let it stop bleeding a second time; or place the point of the flame at the wound until the coagulated blood from the vein flows out, and place a piece of fresh linen on top, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is open, do not restrain it but let it be until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place where it was drawn before, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is connected to the vein of the head because they are composed of the same material.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of the wound is that the patient pushes their hand into boiling hot water, until the flesh becomes red; then it should be tied slightly, so the vein appears clearly; then press gently along the vein, neither wide nor long; and let it be pierced widely, and let the wound be sewn close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand back into boiling hot water, and let the blood flow in the hot water as much as you have; and if it is in the summer, do not push the hand back into boiling hot water again, because it causes more harm in the summer than in winter; and the wound of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The healing of the thumb of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how it's done: strap the hand, immerse it in hot water until the vein swells, if possible to see; and if the thumb is sore, and you cover it completely with hot water, it won't cause any harm; do not push too deep, for the nerves are exposed under the skin all around, then put the hand back into hot water, provided that the wound is not frozen over and cannot heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as needed, put oil and linen on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgation of the left hand's skin is beneficial for the disease of the mice, and do as I told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The healing of the saphena (long vein in the inner lower leg) is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the stomach, retention of fluids, rheumatism, and old legs and knees, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of his wound is that the patient steps on hot water and rubs it over the vein until it burns, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many rain-like lines; therefore open the largest line or one near the ankle, which is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you close it above the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and close it through as in cutting; and let the flames be still.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the wound does not heal, immerse the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the wound needs to be treated the first time, start the second one above a little, because the skin is salty; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the sole of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The area of the sciatic vein is at the ankle joint, and lancing it relieves the pain of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the quality of his wound is that the patient immerses himself in water and twists above the ankle four feet, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, treat it in every way you can, and by crossing over it; and it is more effective to cover it, because the skin is tough and responds poorly to hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't correct it, no remedy will open or close the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of nerves; and make as much incision as you see fit, and then untie the ligament, and put cotton on it and press; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 wounds caused by the cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters (of ventouse) are made of horns, or hog's bristles, or glass; and ventosation is done according to two methods: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 This cupping, which is done by cutting or without fire, has two methods: one that affects the whole body, or with fire; and cupping that is made by cutting and bloodletting is performed in 14 leagues of the body, so that one is completely on the head (the top); and others are in the neck; and others in the two sides of the neck; and cupping under the chin; and cupping under the shoulders; and cupping over the ankles; and cupping in the arms; and cupping in the legs; and cupping in the wrists; and cupping is not used for bloodletting, but only for minor veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it should not be administered at all, neither by fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from swelling, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if due to necessity or custom it is required to use cupping, we shall administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and during any time; for there are those who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and those who find themselves full and red in their face, head, neck, and dark under the eyes; and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, their tongue has swollen and bleed; and those who think, see black spots and hallucinate, and dream and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially during the month, we order to have them bled after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The suction of the nose helps with headaches ... that come under the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this cupping is in place of cephalic bleeding, and it should not be used on those who have a cold constitution or are constipated, as it does great harm to them; and therefore those with head colds or diseases should not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if one heals often from it, they become numb, and therefore, the ventosation must be placed a little lower due to the fear of numbness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is in the position of the spine and basilica, and for this reason it is beneficial for compression of the pains, and for splitting of the channel of the opening, and all of these; and it must be pressed gently, because if it holds too firmly, it causes obstruction or pain in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation in the costal part of the neck is beneficial for pains in the head, and otalgia and emigraine, and for strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the position of the spine of the basilica; and you should command the patient to press gently with his hand, not to crush the artery, and no bleeding should come.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind-tunnels under the chin are useful for mouth diseases, tooth decay, and similar mouth illnesses; they are in the position of the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind-tunnels in the shoulders are useful for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the armpits are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; instruct the lord not to press too deeply, for the flesh is naked there and knows nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventosation on the buttocks is worth as much as the emorroid operations at their foundation, and for diseases below, and it must be large and made of horsehair, which needs to be drawn well, and if it were too thin, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely because they attract blood from all over the body, and they are similar to ancient pains in the sides, hips, and bladder, and they reduce the flow of fluids; they are located at the junctions of the shins and ankles, and they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus into various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to treat the swelling is that you first evacuate it and immediately apply a warm substance, press it quickly, move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the redness and swelling subside, and the redness of the blood appears; then bandage it, and take care in the position of the body, because there are some who have hard flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to wound only once, and it is necessary to make wide incisions, but not too deep; and evacuate gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to make two incisions: the first one to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very thick, it must be struck three times; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we should prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 If we want much blood, let us frequently draw it; if the flesh is thick, press deeply, and set a limit so that the veins are pierced suddenly; it is necessary for those with thick skin and hard who have narrow pores, to anoint the leeks of the armpits with stimulating and dissolving oil: if in summer, use violet oil, sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; if in winter, use oil of parsley, lilies, chamomile, or other similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil or balsam oil, anise oil, and any similar oil.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the patient whose wound you are treating has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after the lancing with rose water, or cold water, or vinegar water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or another similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ashes or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with excessive fluids rise from old wine or sour milk, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar; and no one should be lanced before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after the lancing, and it is necessary that he urinate, when he should be lanced and when he has been lanced.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And keep in mind that the person who is recovering is colicky and too acute and inflamed; therefore, it is necessary for him to take cold things, such as raw apples, endives, lettuces, and similar foods; and eat little, and meat of chicken, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 If the person has a cold complexion, he should take honey syrup, fragrant wine moderately old, and eat little, and eat peas, and finely chopped birds and sparrows; on the day when he vomits, he should drink more than eat; it is necessary to give some men some triacetum or muscatel before or after the vomiting, or afterwards, to strengthen the main limbs; and let the inflamed ones be slightly cooled, but he who is hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The ventouses that are placed to wound are those that are placed on the liver, spleen, gout, belly and side, as these members cannot bear being wounded elsewhere, and this is done only to draw blood from one member into another, for example, on nipples when a woman is nursing; to remove viscosity from the member, as we do with a ventouse on the abdomen or side to reduce it; and to alleviate pain, where there is obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive power accidentally the obstruction, or displaces the stone from its place; and in this way it operates when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness, and these ventouses are administered empty for suctioning only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, such as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a manner one fills the ventouse with hot saline solution or with hot water where herbs such as convulvulus have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the blister to be treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and a half palm's width apart, and have a hole of the size of a small nail, like pushing an awl, and made of iron, soft beforehand so as not to prick the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle, there should be a rod of a span in length, either of iron or steel, for placing a splint, and they should be big and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for children's boils are different from old people's, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this boil splint should be placed on the limb: take a linen or wax strip and place it across the rod within the boil, so that the light is at the bottom of the boil to prevent burning the patient; then place the splint on the limb, and the fingers should be above the hole as we have said, so that when one looks, if steam comes out, the boil can be removed; and take a linen strip again as before, and apply it frequently, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder, which is administered when there is pleurisy disease, it has no worm nor puncture, and it is not administered except when it is full of liquid, and it is placed on the member only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Snaives are not administered except in members where bladders cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in naked skin areas, such as the palms or soles, and others of this kind; and the quality of the user is that when you find snaives that are in clear, sweet, net liquid, take them; put them in a sweet, clear container until they become familiar and have nothing in their bellies; then let it be sanitized with wine and bladder, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the snaives on it; and when they are full and warm, if it is a place where a bladder can be placed, put the bladder there, for this works very well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If it is not so, lift the shoulder blade slightly, then more strongly, very well, and press on it; if the shoulders are still too close to the body after the ribs, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, place it, until the ribs are dry; if the ribs multiply, place broken vitriol or salve, or similar things, until they are dry; or you place half-peeled beans on the shoulder blade and leave them until they harden onto the shoulder blade, it will be healed now; and if you have more need of this, take other ribs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 If the ribs do not want to be taken, rub the shoulder blade with fresh blood or insert an awl until the ribs come out, then place them, and as soon as they feel blood, they will harden; when you see that they are dislocated, sprinkle some powder of aloe and soap, or charcoal on it, and it will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn, dear child, that the foolish man should abandon this chapter, for he will never see any of the ancient books, nor read any letters from them; and because of this, science is alienated in our land, for I have never found good one; and I do not know anything more, except by the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book the number of words and the chapters where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When fracture, dislocation, twisting or sprain comes to anyone, you should hurry to heal the patient on both sides, if nothing prevents it, such as frailty of body, weakness, or old age; or if the time is not very hot, or too cold; and you should eat cool foods, that is to say cold meats, and meat of eye and shin, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not eat too many foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about an abscess being hot, or spreading matter to the member; if the patient returns to his first good government as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause thick mucus, such as cooked wheat in water and broth, meat, heads, feet, beef, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For thick nourishment strengthens and heals the broken bones more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well regained nor joined according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, neither those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, set the large tenons on the fractured bone which fits and joins the limb together, until it is enforced as before; and do not apply any pressure to the joint, and therefore feed it with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the foot, or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the joint, and another growing sharper, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a break with a wound, then it is a break with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each one has its tool and instrument appropriate for restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the joint is twisted and opened wide, and pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no breakage; but it may have twisting, or fissuring, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move the hand yourself, but put on the medicines that come after this, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the breaks that go to the elbow, and are the two parts disjointed, they should now be put back in alignment equally, otherwise abscesses may grow there; and if abscesses grow there, let it rest for a day until the abscess is soothed; then place it equal to the arm that you can easily and wisely move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one where it has been broken into pieces; then tighten as needed.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 If the bone is broken into pieces, it should be set with two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or in your hand it is a small member, or two cords, or one cord and in your hand; then place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are dislocated, you restore them using all means necessary, ensuring not to cause injury or pain to the patient. Align the two joints of the bone well according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems not well to you: straighten it properly, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it by their work abscess heat and contraction to the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is set, correctly bind the patient so that he does not move, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and be careful that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 If it feels no pain, then the limb is not set, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain; be careful that it is straightened, so that twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs can be of various kinds, large or small, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For small members such as fingers and thumbs: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and thin linen cloths; for larger ones such as hands and legs: it is necessary to wrap with a wide and stiff rope, because the large ropes embrace the whole large limb equally, and they keep it straight without any twist; then wrap around light bandages, three or four times according to the member, and hold tight one part of the rope with your hand; then go above the fracture and tighten less than the fracture, pull away slightly from the fracture; and soften the rope little by little until you take a large piece of healthy flesh; then take another rope, and twist it around the other way over the broken limb; then return to the lower part of the fracture, and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor loosely as we have said in the first rule above; then put between the ropes soft bandages until they are all even; then bind everything together with tape, and then make well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is an inflammation or abscess, place a soothing substance for the abscess that is hot over it, and let the inflammation be for certain days; then press on your elbows, and they should be half the thickness of a large cane carefully sawn, or a rod used to make fissures, or palm reeds, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But the elbows that one places over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and they should also be as long as the member is small or large; then press on the elbows in the same way as you did at the first instruction, then tie a cord above it accordingly, as in the first instruction over the fracture; the cord should be narrower here, then wider again; and it should be medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax yarn; because if the cord is too thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their knots from twisted flax, and this is a great error, because the knot cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each elbow.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of arrows after resetting the shoulder in a healthy state, place linen or linen bandages under them so they do not fester.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the veins are broken, I will tell the cure afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know this: it is not necessary to bind all broken limbs tightly on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, no need to apply hot irons before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your confidence in the abscess healing; and here is the ancient method for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that is held on the mill walls, and mix it with abundant egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, into use, and this is the common method of healing fractures in various ways, and especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take aloes, linseed oil, turpentine, balm of Gilead, mastic, in equal amounts; myrrh and aloeswood, 5 times the amount; and seven times as much alum; make powder from them, mix with enough egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and it benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method for healing twisting: take mugwort and mastic, mix 10 parts; mirrh and aloes, mix 9 parts; acacia 6 parts; Armenian bole 10 parts, grind well, and mix with vinegar or abundant egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of splinting for joints and dislocated bones, soothing the pain that occurs, and reducing it with a chisel and breaking: take new linen, wet it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the joint or bone.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore [the damage], but it is good for soothing abscess heat and proper bone pain.
