Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster for broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthy parsley, grind them together to make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of plaster for the healing of a broken bone and to hasten the healing of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of vismalve, camomile, viola flowers, powder of beech leaves, each one part; grind them and mix with wine, and if the limbs are scalded, mix it with coriander water or vinegar and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of application stronger than the first, when the abscess hard comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of comfrey, flax, balm of Gilead, lupine, and wild cucumber, and flowers of violets and camomile, all in one part; grind, and concoct with vinegar, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that nothing but a beeswax and oil ointment should be put on the broken member for restoration, and no other thing more, and says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should place warm, slightly dry things on the broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat a wound and pain: take ground mugwort and horse hooves that have been boiled, or feathers of birds, and sow thistle, equal amounts, grind them and make a poultice out of it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then release the joint a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if it does not release on its own. Release it by hand, but if pain comes to the place, or swelling, without rest or inflammation, hasten, and release it, and remove the dislocated cartilage immediately; take a light cloth, and a damp sponge of the sea, dip it in water, and lift up the joint, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is relieved; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen moistened with water or rose oil on it, and tie it with a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is heated; and soothe the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then start the subtle reduction again, a little at a time, and not too forcefully as before; and reduce it gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess swells and reddens and hurts, and it needs to be lanced and sutured, proceed as you did the first time equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no inflammation comes to the limb as we have said, do not dislocate it before three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the break heals and approaches the joint with flesh; then hold it longer than before, and let the tissue thicken its meat, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot enter therein; therefore, moisten it with warm water, every third day, and loosen a little the bandage; by this means cut off the nourishment from the limb, and hasten healing of what the foolish surgeon allows to remain twisted: this is bad, and it is an unsafe practice, and I see nothing but laziness and working incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist and have various shapes, and their causes are specific; for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the shaft breaks the entire bone up to the shaft that is beneath the bone, as happens with a hack or cleaver; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hackure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	when the sword strikes the bone from above it pierces through, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and these two types of fractures are either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion filled, or cut, or from wounds of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the break penetrates through to the membrane under the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if the wound is sunk into the bone as thinly as a hair, and it has a small crack, then this type of fracture is called "capillare"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, falling, or similar things, and makes the bone piece enter below, and the ends of the bone are cut like blacksmiths do when they hammer on cauldrons; where the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have a moist head bone, as in the case of a child's skull; and it occurs in all these ways of fracture where small parts are dislocated, such as splinters; and I will speak about it later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of breaks through dissection above them, and the examination by probing, and the corruption of the flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known to those who, when the bone has been exposed and rubbed inward, if it opens the black crack will appear.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful about the patient's condition, and if you see any harmful symptoms like vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, fainting, high fever, hairs falling out and turning red, and other similar signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptoms and hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth moon within which you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is corrupted, and come the events we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the fracture of the bone reaches up to the skin that covers the brain, you must cut the fractured part as follows: it is necessary to grab the patient's head firmly, and expose the bone on all sides in any way you can, and over the figure of the wound more gently than you can; and if drainage of blood comes out to expose the bone, or pus accumulates, assist with whatever is needed; and fill the area with dampened linen soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the pus subsides and be sure there is no more bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you make a deep notch in front, and it is called the oblique way.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made with iron instruments; and work lightly, so that you do not wound the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is protruding and hard, you must pierce around it, so that you administer incisions with drills, not cutting through the bone of the head, but having a margin or circle above the point to prevent the drill from passing through the bone; and you must have several, so that each one comes in its place along the length of the bone, so that you have drills for all sides; and this is the shape of the four types of drills.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are that you place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the drill to another part a little afterwards, and do this all around, then remove the chips of the bone that are between the holes, and do this as delicately and lightly as possible, as we have said, until you pull out the bone or any of the instruments you have such as pliers or forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you retract the fragment that remains of the bone to all other similar instruments, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors; and if something remains of the small bones or scales, gently remove them with the tools; then cure the wound with cauterization and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Greeks call (it), which is more reliable; and it is highly praised, and this is its statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you must expose part of the bone where the fracture is visible, so that when you have exposed that part, place it under the tip of the chisel-like instrument as shown in this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 Do not cut in one part, and the fragment should be split into two sides, so that the saw is toward the bone; then strike with a small hammer so you lightly split the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is beneath; if it is attached to the bone, gently remove it, for it is often broken without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the fracture does not pierce through to the cloth and the bone is only chopped from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smooth that roughness, and remove scales with a sharp scraper of various sizes, in order to provide the most suitable amount, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	The patient should shave his head completely first with a large razor, then with finer ones afterwards, and continue to do so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other kind of haircut and subtle break, you must bring the instrument according to his discretion; and this is not a matter that can be answered by one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is open, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled over once or twice, wet it with wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as possible, so as not to burden the wound, then administer more linen over it but do not tie it too tight that it only covers the wound; and leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess subsides, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily root, oat flour, incense powder, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, and administer immediate medications without poisoning; and ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or pus, because when pus gathers on the linen cloth, it will rot and decay, causing great harm to the patient; for when something sharp is put on the wound, it may rot from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, this is cause for doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness does not come violently except for medicine that has been applied there, it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in wax the cloth, and put it on top; then treat it with methods of treatments as necessary until it heals completely.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, or one part alone, because there are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 If one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you grind your little finger or thumbnail and equal the breakage inside your index finger cavity, and at the knuckle by pressure, until the nail grows again according to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, you should place a small stick equal to the height of the root of the finger there.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If the breakage is in two parts, do the same, and hasten to restore it the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day when the abscess has calmed down, then insert linen thread tentatively at the root of the nail where the breakage is.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place another on the other side if there is a break there; and let the bandages be as thick as they fill the neck openings.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said any remedy that one must soak the tents in butter and churn them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems not to be good, but it is required that they should be soaked in a concoction of egg yolk and flour powder; then leave the tendon until the bone becomes hard, and the cartilages become tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers from an owl are put in place of tents, and if it is covered with a thin cloth, and the opening is held closed, breath the patient through; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes out while you are working on it, put beeswax or cotton wool soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of sulphur there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If abscesses do not come, apply an ointment on the outside, made from flour of wheat and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then put light bandages on it and do not bind it too tightly; if the break in the bone is small and broken into many pieces, remove them using suitable tools, then stitch the wound, and treat the injured flesh, healing, and sewing, as ointments and ointments appropriate for that purpose; and if there is no injury inside the bone, cure the tendon, and put cotton plugs in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	on the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated beneath [something], and there is no wound outside, and the break is only outside, but not broken through, unless hollow inside, it can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the break is in the left mandible, insert your index finger of the right hand and gently push it inside, then adjust it evenly with the other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the mandible is dislocated at two joints, then you must administer extension of two parts until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or rupture, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place a bandage on the broken jaw and place .i. double cloth over it; and place over the cloth a large well-made splint, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and attach it above the muzzle that you can, and command the patient to rest, and nourish light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, dislocate it on the third day and then reposition what has changed; place a plaster over it with flour from the mill mixed with egg or flour from a sieve, after you have removed the bandage; and place light linen over the plaster, and if the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it heals within four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come up, bring what we have said before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, observe that no piece of the bone has been removed; it requires subtle instruments suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrowed, expand (it) with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all the pieces and none remain, then stitch (the) wound if it is wide, and place on it one plaster suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks multiple times towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when there is a fracture with an open wound, that you have two attendants, one holding the shoulder where the force breaks, and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then place the dislocation in your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to extend further, place a round ball of fabric or linen over the patient's shoulder, as thick as necessary; stretch and tie the force (the fracture), hold the ball with your hand, and align the dislocation as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outwards due to it being fully closed, then the patient must lie on their affected side and place one hand under the shoulder; and push the shoulder downwards, until the bones of the socket are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find debris, then it is necessary that you cut across [the bone]; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join due to any hindrance, then crush it at one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to hold it in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it seems like a spoon, and is not hollow, and should be as large as needed, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two openings, as you see, and one wide, and the other narrow, as the wound is when treating the bones; and when you are certain that it is an abscess, cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt that it is an abscess, use cloths and linen, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if it is hot abscesses that come, soak one linen cloth in rose oil, asafetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the bone when it has wounds and incisions is to put a plaster of mill powder and egg yolk on the bone, and place light bandages over it, and if you need it, place a splint under the affected area; then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, put two layers of cloth over the bandages, and the plaster; then take a thin stick of three feet long and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang out; and place the stick over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the affected shoulder and the affected arm; and tighten each part separately, and when you see that the fracture heals properly and you can clearly see that the stick does not move from the broken bone, keep it in place every day, and when the ligaments loosen, tighten it again; and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the affected area to raise the shoulder; if the fracture aligns with the force of the shoulder through the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it except for bad accidents, until twenty days have passed; then resume plastering, if needed, and tighten it and leave it in place until it is healed; and it will be healed most in twenty-eight days, and less with some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates and one cannot move it except through touch; then one arranges it according to the shape of the break, and sets it back in place according to its natural form in all possible ways; then put powder from the mill on top with a lot of egg and light splints, and cover it with double cloth; then put a large and thin needle over it, about a little larger than the shoulder, and if there are any humps anywhere on the shoulder, use linen splints to fill them so that the needle becomes smooth; and then tie it all firmly in one great bind, so that the needle does not move from its place, and watch the ligament every day; and each time it softens, tighten it, and make the needle equal if it is out of its place, and lay the patient on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. When this number is reached, loosen it, and be careful because it is not easy for a bone to become dislocated lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone part protrudes in front and not under the skin, lift it up and cut it, and do as we have said to treat an abscess using hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture (the) thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The fracture is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks near the edge.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 When it is broken in the middle, it sinks downward and causes the patient great pain, without help, immediately, and sometimes blood comes out from the fractured bones, and the fracture is opened widely, and everything hurts a lot.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on their back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two costal arches with both hands, subtlety adjusting it to be even in all ways possible, until the figure of the bone is as required; then put pressure bandages and poultices made of salt or a lighter material, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the limb round repeatedly, and tighten it gently, and examine every hour if it softens, if it becomes soft then tighten it again; and if it requires dislocation due to corrosion or itching at the location, or pain or abscess, hurry up, and dislocate it, remove the pressure bandage, and treat the one who has come with remedies of cures; then reset the pressure bandage and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the ribs fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Note that the fracture of the ribs occurs only in large ones posterior to the back and at the neck inside, and they bend only because they are slippery; and it is well felt in the examination of the hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then put the plaster and bind with a stick if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is inclined inside, the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, like pleurisy, for the bone pierces the flesh; the armpits swell, and they immediately vomit a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients have made many efforts to cure it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, in order to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not allow hot irons to come if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have come, make it healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said one of us puts blisters on the limb to ripen it, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the blisters attract excessive fluid to the limb due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said one should cover the limb with damp linen dipped in hot oil and place poultices between the ribs to make the swelling equal around it, then let it be treated with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the fractured bone and there is doubt in the patient's mind, then it is necessary to make an incision on the side of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place instruments under it for support; and then you must cut the bone, draw it out gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plaster until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess comes, lay it on soft cloth soaked in rose oil and place it there; and cure the side of it that needs to be treated with abscess, and lie it often on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes breaks occur in the bones of the neck, and sometimes it bends; and similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when it happens to someone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in many positions, and if it does not move or feel when you strain and prick it, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient should be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if something similar happens in the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, take care if the feet are soft, and if accidents happen that are in hands, and above the back there is a sudden jump and evacuation without willing; and when it is put on the stomach, it jumps again without willing.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is placed on the back and it wants to sit down, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is fatal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward [the patient] if there is an abscess that is hot, you place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then put one of the soothing and drying plasters on top, bind it with a string, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he recovers.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, you must cover it with oil; then remove the bone, join the two edges of the wound together with a stitch, if it is large, until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," put your left thumb in its place and hold it equal to your right hand, then apply the plaster and splint, if necessary; then tighten it, and if any bone dislocates again, you must fix it, remove the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it occurs, there is only a little lessening at the head; it becomes long, bends towards the groin, and comes to the patient pain at the place where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break; and recognize what the break is and the shape of it; and if the break is only at the head, then make the break equal to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it bends inside, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of that break is presented to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, place the splint on it, then place a stick or a yew branch on top and hold the fracture so it does not move; and press the joint beneath the ribs until they are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has broken out, do not touch it until it is soothed, and place what we have previously mentioned on top of it; then return to treatment, and hold it as needed, if there is no bad event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	the shoulder blade is that which is between the ribs and the neck of the upper arm, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two manners: one of which is that you take a rod thicker than your little finger, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads together with two rods, and pass them over the top, and place the patient on one seat; then lower his broken arm onto the rod, until it reaches the shoulder joint, and attach a splint of rod in the middle, then raise it above some heavy object or have the ministers extend it below; then place the mirrors the breaker's hands together, until the breaker returns as required.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way it is that one binds the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one holds where it is above the break with his hands, and the others hold below all the way, and each extends to their respective parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 If you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder joint, you must put a splint beneath it and on the other side, below the break; and in the same way, if the break is toward the outside, you should put a light splint without effort, until the break is even with the joint and with the skin; then make it equal and hold it, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does come, do not hold it for more than 7 days, and put soft linen with rose oil on it until the abscess is soothed; then hold it, and the method of holding it is that you place a plaster on the break, then raise the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and hold the cloth, and hold it on the shoulder, and on the arm, such that the arm is in a straight line, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint above the fracture, with one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to pass over the fracture by two inches on each side; then hold the splints as I have said at the beginning of the chapter regarding the fracture, more firmly and less in loosening.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 If you see the swelling and constriction, as we have said, during the process of restoring a broken limb, and you doubt an abscess has formed, leave it to heal for seven days as we have said; then examine every three days the bandage, to ensure that pus does not swell or come to the area, nor the nails become too tight on the limb because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if such an accident does not occur, it should not be dislocated before three days or more, and the patient should lie on his back and have his hands on his stomach; and put beneath the shoulder a cushion filled with equal wool, and observe every hour of the day or night whether the figure of the broken limb moves or the tendons are softened; if it is immobile by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have mentioned earlier, in such a way that the meat is first tender; and when it begins to heal, it should become large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be set right within 40 days altogether; and then you must dislocate it and administer baths and ointments to straighten it.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 If the structure (joint) is deformed and swollen, it takes days or two months to dislocate it.
de la brisure du bras	Of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones which are called the "forearm," of which one is small and it's the one that forms the wrist; and the other is large, and it's the one that is below, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large forearm can break, or only the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When small bladder stones are broken, the restoration (treatment) is easy, and healing is quick; but when large ones are broken, healing is poor, and it hurts more than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small bladder stone is broken, it should be gently stretched out and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large bladder stone that is broken, it must be tightened more strongly; stretch it up over the funnel (a device used during urinary stone removal), and bend the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the others, and the patient should cross his arms over himself and the funnel above him to prevent any pain; then the attendant should extend his arm to the part below, where he holds the patient's hand or rope, and another attendant extends his arm above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then set the limb even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is a fracture in several pieces, put each one back into its place; and if there is any displacement that pierces the skin which you cannot restore to its place, cut off and remove the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it is with the break causing an open wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; take care for its treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if at the beginning of treatment abscesses appear, apply a plaster made of rose oil and white beeswax, neither too hard nor too soft; and attach the plaster carefully until the abscesses subside.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the plaster, and apply a poultice of flour milled with egg, then place the splints, and let the splint from the fracture be stronger and slightly wider than the others; and know that it should have six splints or more in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less on the sides, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard or dry; and let the thread, which holds it together, be of linen, not too thick or thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And hold the member and the limb for some days after.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 If any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that happens on the member, then you must irrigate the member with hot water until the itching is eased; and allow the member not to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then begin the binding, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones dislocated, as well as anything similar, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the urine cannot reach the limb because it is too narrow, then you must soften it for a short while and let it be for some days until the urine flows through it, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things mentioned above come to the patient, do not remove the dressing for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 If it is an injury around the neck, hold his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and keep him from movement and tilting; sleep on his back. Know that this break will heal in thirty or thirty-five days, and sometimes in twenty, depending on the compositions and complexions of the properties.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	In the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few breaks, and they occur many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or fractured, the patient should lie flat on his back and stretch out straight in front of him equally; then place his hand above a cloth and extend the broken bones, aligning them with mirrors, until they are well joined; apply a plaster and wadding if an abscess does not appear, then apply a splint according to the size of the fracture; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the back of the sole near the belly of the foot, make a splint from cloths and instruct the patient to strap his broken foot to it; then fasten a long cloth, and the splint should be as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is open, then you should place a splint above and another one below in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and compress the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If a fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, you should make it even as necessary; and hold it with the sole, and if you see that you place a straight small splint to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, you should make them even, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie all of them in one place, which is better, or place a splint on it, as for the thumb; and take care in the restoration and placement of the abscess heat, and treat those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	fractured shin
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the shin are often broken, and it is easily seen when they twist forward and backward; and the restoration [of the bone] is that one tie [a splint] is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then each minister extends their tie evenly to their respective parts; and this is when the break is at the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the leg, it should be one of the joints toward the ankle, and the other joints below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is near the knee, then it should be the joints below the knee, and the extension beyond; then set the bone equal to its two hands, according to its natural figure, and then apply the splint, and the bandage, unless an abscess comes.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess heated (treated with heat), let it be allowed to cool down before returning to your work and treatment; the procedure is carried out in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You should cover the break with a bandage double in one or three layers, and keep the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the groin, and pass the thread long between the leg and thigh, below the knee, and bring the ends of the thread above; then turn the leg and the bandage upwards, then put supports on the break and a support on the bone of the leg; then use a strip of soft cloth for the strapping, to equalize the tension, then begin to tie three or four turns around the break; and as you go higher from the break, loosen it less; then take the two threads that you passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three supports on top, then return to below the end of the thread, so that you come down to the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as it is, unless an abscess or swelling or any other similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a swelling or any piece of the bone that protrudes, you should cut it off if possible; and if not, you should break the area and draw out the pus; and treat it as we have said before until it heals completely.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the leg is broken in such a way as if one sets a splint, as in the shoulder or arm; however, during restoration, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the leg is restored within one day, or a little more or less, according to the differences in complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the leg (genuine)
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not really broken, but rather a crack or piercing, and there is pain in every place, and this hurts a lot.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: When equalizing the bone that is broken to its place, it should be assembled as much as possible; then put the splint, and place a round stick there if needed, and hold it in place as necessary, then check all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as abscess heat and similar things; apply to each accident what is required, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called the shinbone or "mustelz," and the other is called the fibula; and it breaks similarly to the arm, and therefore the repair is the same as for the arm, and the treatment is the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg twists in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 If the large bone is broken, there is great pain, and it can be seen; and it turns underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply extension, make it even, and tie the sticks equally; however, if the fracture is crooked, and there are more pieces, let the extension be smaller and lighter; align accordingly to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two handfuls of straw that cover the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap it in two layers, one on top and one underneath, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and this is good; and no one should place one bandage of the length of the leg, and it should be of straw, and place the leg for protection against movement, and do this at the break where there is pain; move the leg every day to see if there is abscess or other accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break of bones, but at times there is a break in the foot and toes, and it does not occur often except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the foot bones, and you see these bones rising one above the other, put the patient on his back on the ground, as if he wants to go, then place your foot on top of the injured one where the bones have risen, then press it until they return to their place; then apply a splint and bandage, and put a small plank under the foot with two flat pieces, then tighten the bandage around the foot in the usual way, after you have wrapped fabric around it, and other things that are needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the bandage as you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said about the hand bones; then set a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and it should be slightly larger, then place a table beneath the splinted area as I have said, and apply pressure as needed; and if there are more than 2, or 3, or more broken bones, set a splint on each one according to their quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the table beneath the splinted area; and it should be positioned so that it covers the belly of the bone, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not neglect the other things I have said about other fractures, after what has been said; and treat each case according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.
