If the bone of a woman's body is broken, let her sit upright, then lean it to the small of her back and hold it from behind; then fill the wound with cotton for the patient and put as much cotton as needed inside; then press the woman down, and lift the buttock little by little, then pull the cotton out until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and let the bone return with the stick; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or so: the fracture will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder of barley straw, tie one end of a string to it, and insert the whole bladder into the wound; then blow strongly through the string until the bladder is inflated inside: the bone will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone at the elbow of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the humerus bone; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from him who applies his study and skill to them, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 Breaks indicate in various ways the right way of restoration: therefore read on.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for 3 or more days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For that one who has breakage with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or something similar, he must be bandaged now, so that the bandages that we have said bear witness to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, then anoint it with vinegar, if you do not have anything else, then proceed to restore the breakage in that same hour, or on that day, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would cause a bad event to happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed at the edge of the wound, you must gently set it in place with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the fractured bone pieces do not align themselves to be set in place by your hands, you must use this instrument which is made of iron, about 7 or 8 inches long, and as wide as the size of the wound; and for this reason, the mirror should grasp 3 or 4 (depending on what is required in each case of fracture), and it should be round and somewhat large but not too thin so that it does not bend during your work on the limb, and it should be sharp at the front end and thick from the middle to the tip, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "humerus", because the curved head of the bone must be placed on top of the visible part of the bone; and push it once, until it returns to its original position, and ensure that one side is equal to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 If the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone, you must cut the head of the bone so that the instrument has enough power to do it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your power; then remove that which is left in the bone by sharp cutting and small scrapes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Then place it in its natural position, moisten the linen cloth with black stitched wine if it is summer, and not on oil or any other substance that may cause corruption on the wound; afterwards administer medicine when you have reset the bone, leave the wound exposed, and cover it around according to the size of the wound, taking care that the wound is not constricted by the fracture; many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, causing either death or corruption for the patient, and therefore, let the bandage be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, do not put stitches on it; but wrap around, in place of stitches, hard bandages, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And if the following day or two you notice pus forming on the wound, remove what you have put on it and apply healing salve for wounds, such as treacle of antimony and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, at morning and evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be placed so that the bone moves down gently towards the inside.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but goes down again, since there are small fragments of bones, you must try to cure the wound and remove all those loose fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 If a fistula (or another form of corruption) appears at the place, you must treat it, as he has said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 If the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bone, or other similar large bones, do not try to draw it out because many times death comes from it; but leave it until it can be pulled; perhaps it will shrink in about 20 or 30 days. Then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving blisters on the sores
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are often many times after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an unpleasant sight to see the shape of the limb; and unfortunately, the limbs cannot perform their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, be careful if we are sick: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and saracocola, acacia, and similar ones; so take any of these things or all together, and grind them with a sharp vinegar or with enough egg white or oil; then place it on the wound in poultices, and hold it tightly and do not remove it for many days; and then open it, and start another one, until the node is removed; or you can apply a well-made wooden plank, because the properties of wood are that it removes all inflammations from limbs. If the node has turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then you chop it off with a knife, and make the excess apparent; or you scrape it with any rasp, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak limb after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the broken bone is restored and remains weak and fragile afterwards, this happens for many reasons: one of them being that it was tied too tightly, not as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, preventing the nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or due to excessive movement, not in its hour; or due to a lack of blood in the body, causing it to be weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body lean until the blood is multiplied in him; administer a bath, give joy and comfort; then put wax on the limb so that the wax attracts great nourishment to it, and let the swelling be often reduced with cold water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is disfigured, yet it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and possibly death. Yet, if the swelling and pain are fresh, they must be treated with hot, cooling water or softening herbs such as comfrey leaves, roots, medicks, etc.; make one poultice made of a mollifying substance like daisy, and take the musk of comfrey, mix it with gelatin oil or sesame oil, and make a poultice. Or you can make a poultice from ripe figs ground with wheat bran, etc., and similar medicines that alleviate the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes, the dislocation is removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And movements should be brought to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is swollen and hardened, like stone, and it requires to be cut with iron, it should be covered up to the bone, at the subtle incision gently made; and apply cushion and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, it must now be reset carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one waits, the limb swells, and in case it is reset at that time; therefore, it should not be moved until it has diminished: many times it causes pus and other pain; however, when this happens, let the patient cleanse himself, then leave him, until the abscesses have subsided; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently stretch it, and treat each limb as needed according to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated in several ways; and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are slightly dislocated from their places, becoming somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and the saliva flows out of the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it returns through multiple positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is complete and finished, then you must quickly reset it, without delay, and in such a way that the minister grabs the head of the patient, and pushes one of his fingers from one hand into the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other hand should be spread open, to make it even; and instruct the patient to soften, his lower jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror (or instrument) should make it even until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaws (or broken bones) are dislocated, apply hot water and oil to them, moving them gently until they are reset; do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they [the dislocated joints] are reset equally, and the patient closes the mouth well with a soft poultice made of rose oil and wax, then place it lightly on several bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders between two cushions so that he does not move either to the right or left, nor forces himself in any way, but takes light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws [shoulders] are healed; then gradually eat what he wants lightly, and do not force himself to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaws are completely healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set right within an hour and are not turned to their places, fevers and accustomed sweats occur, and possibly the rupture of the stomach, and by chance, the vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a disaster; and many times he who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot dislocate towards the chest or the hip, and it dislocates sometimes outwards, and one can feel this happening.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoring [of dislocated joints] is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then presses the joint firmly with his palm, and it will return; then apply the bandage and bind it; and the shoulder which is towards the costal region cannot dislocate again; if not, and if it dislocates once, reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the bandage and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way, the shoulders of the back are restored when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder dislocates in only three ways: one is when it dislocates at the top part of the socket joint beneath; the second is at the hip joint; and by chance it may dislocate above the hip joint, which rarely happens; it does not dislocate behind the shoulder or inside the nerves; and it often dislocates below the socket towards the shoulder, especially in those with little flesh, as it easily goes back into place; but in those with enough flesh, it jumps back to its place with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess hot, and thinks that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must check, as long as you are sure; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocations when going towards the shoulder, there is a difference between the sick and healthy shoulder, and you will find differences between them; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below the socket at the point of the top of the shoulder, as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring his hand to its place nor make any movements; and similarly, when dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will perceive it clearly on touch; and this manner of dislocation is not easily remedied, when it is new, or when the nerves are weak.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places his thumb under the joint, and forcibly bends the joint upward to its place; the minister then lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back; it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in the hands on certain days afterwards, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and provide them with soothing and softening medicine such as a concoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and it should be given to them; then place the patient on their back, and put a piece of linen equal in size beneath the affected shoulder, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of another person on the linen, and carefully lift the head of the shoulder; and another person holds the hand of the patient, so that it does not move downwards; that shoulder immediately returns to its place, and if you see it dislocating again in this manner: then ensure a person who is larger than the patient is present; and be facing towards their side, and push the affected shoulder beneath the patient's affected shoulder, and lift the affected shoulder upwards so the patient hangs in the air; and another person pulls the patient's hand downwards towards their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, he cannot bear any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 It is also done in another way: it is when a long thorn is placed into the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is as round as a pea and not too big or too small; then it is placed under the patient with cloths soft on top, and the patient lies along the pole; then his hand is extended on the other side in this manner, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, perform this cure: take a thorn from two strong branches and four finger-widths wide, which has the tip rounded to be inserted deeply under the ascle, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the rod on top of the head covered with the cloth so that it does not prick the patient, then place him under the patient's ass; extend one arm over the rod and fasten the shoulder to the rod, and hold the hand at the end of the arm, then place the arm on one side of a wide yoke, and extend the other hand below; leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in its place, in whatever way that may be, you must put a equal length of wool under the ass; then apply a plaster made from mill powder, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then bind it under the ass accordingly, and turn the string around the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats little food, until the limb is comforted, because it will heal faster; and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it becomes hard and is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is moved out of its place by moisture or for any other reason, then you must administer fire cautery at three places, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint cannot stay in place or lift the arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is pinched or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation that is towards the hip or backside is caused by an impact and stretching of hands, and other methods are applied for its treatment; it should be treated until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if afterwards, when the member is healed, there comes swelling and slow movement, the patient should use baths many times until the swelling subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	The cost of dislocation is...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint is dislocated at the point, and it returns to the point; and if it has dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired, because it can be seen well and felt well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when joining the broken bone with the healthy one, make sure you can see them clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is swollen and cannot bend the arm nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as soon as the abscess comes to be open, for if the abscess comes to be open, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset completely, especially when it is at the back; it is worth more than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps there comes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that you extend your two hands to it; its arms should be spread out, and its hands according to the bone all around, above and below, and push the joint back to its places together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and bites the root of the palm that has been dislocated. (Translated line-by-line)
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is best if two people extend the arm, and two apply oil to the joint to soften it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double-folded cloth around it; and when the eyes join the joint to their hand, anoint it with some oil for softening, then push the joint together firmly until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply dry plaster with egg, and hold it firmly, and let the arm hang from the neck of the patient for several days, then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is closed in its place, remove the bandage and leave it as it is; if you see that the joint does not bind well, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then remove the bandage.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if there is pain after the resetting of the joint and it becomes stiff, bathe and scrub it well, press until it is soothed; or you put a sheep's wool grease on the jointure, then leave it for a day and night, then remove it, and make it enter the water; and when it weeps, wipe the jointure gently, then replace the wool, and then enter it in the water again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, put warm moist hay straw on it with butter and apply pressure; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocations of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and it returns easily, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place as quickly as possible, immediately when it is dislocated, unless the muscles are swollen or there is hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the repositioning should be done by placing the affected hand on a table, and extending the fingers of the minister, and aligning the injured hand so that its palm is above the appearance of the jointure, and press it until it returns to its original position; then you must observe if it is correctly placed; then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's palm on the table and have them place their hand above the affected joint area.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it's fine; if not, apply pressure to soothe abscesses with poultices, and let him feel the beginning of relief.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 If he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back after some days, the dislocation remains twisted, causing the patient no benefit as long as his hand is numb and unable to exert any force; then understand that the nerve or artery has been cut; there is no other remedy but to straighten by cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at its place, put the plaster as we have said on it, then hold it and leave for 5 days, then remove it and leave in this manner.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well and there is no pain, apply warm moist cloth and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of fingers in the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the thumb of the hand is dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then stretch it, and push the dislocation towards your pocket until it returns, then hold the head of the thumb, and turn it towards the part where it was disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then make it equal to that day; and tie it, as we have said, and untie it by a day, and make it move, and reattach it; and do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and do the same, when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The displacement of the vertebra of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or neck is dislocated, or when there are multiple dislocations without treatment, the patient quickly dies.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the excrement jumps spontaneously, cannot be held, and many times, any member is softened, or both knees or the two arms or legs; sometimes the spine becomes mute in four parts; the one which becomes mute at the rear is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you observe if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has not, there is no remedy nor healing for it from the beginning.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which falls down or from blows or similar things, the old healers used to say the methods of cures with great words, but there is no benefit in all; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the gilbositeit that comes before, there is neither trick nor health; and similarly, the one that comes straight on two sides, and cannot be cured except by the one that comes at the back, as I have said; and it is that the patient should lie flat in a single place, and have restraint underneath him, so he does not bleed; then insert the iron rod into the head in the earth, and another into the limbs, and tie a rope over the patient's body, and another around the ankles, and knees, and wrists; and two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the others at the limbs, between the two iron rods; and they should be well tightened, the rods as we have said, and the attendants place their palms on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return by this cure, take a board that is three arms long and flat underneath, and the patient should be on their side. Push the head of the board beneath them. Then place the middle of the board upon the spine; place the hands on the other end of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place; if you see that it does not, do it at the turning point which turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And take two needles of a large arm's length, and place them on the patient's head, one on each side, with a palm's length between each needle; and have a notch in each needle where the turn can be, and ensure that the needles are firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between the two needles have a turning needle, like how links turn, and have two small needles of a palm's length on the turning needle to turn it; then tie the cord that is among the ankles to the turning needle towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet at the other turning needle, and each of the assistants turns their turning needle according to the cord, and the master adjusts the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is healed (the dislocation), place a drying plaster on it with much egg white, then press it, then apply the iron rod of three feet long, which penetrates the hollow part of the joint and the healthy part of the vertebra, then tie it with a cord as we have said, and use subtle medicines to keep it healthy until it is healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, administer soothing and softening medicines, with the iron rod as mentioned above; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes the appearance is in the back vertebra of the spine, and it is thought to be dislocation; and this is the bone that opens up, for which one should not have any presumption: perhaps death may come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of the dislocations of the neck
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the dislocations of the neck and shoulder come from nothing but dislocations solely, not otherwise as in other joints; and the joint of the neck is dislocated along four parts: inside and outside, front and back, more inside than otherwise, and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open at the knee for the sick than the healthy; and the sick cannot double their knees in fire; and it is the joint that is dislocated swollen with abscess that is hot, because the heads of the thigh come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this coming outward, it is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of this happening in front are that his leg is well positioned according to the completion; however, do not double the knee due to pain, and if you want him to walk, he cannot move forward, and retains urine, and inflames the ankle, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of this happening behind are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and the leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thighbone is in its place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this kind of dislocation are as follows: you should verify if the dislocations are old and remain according to their position without any treatment; there is no need for presumptions.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those whose dislocation is fresh and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, you should hasten to turn the joint, pushing it inward and outward, and moving it from right to left; possibly it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must summon a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly in his hands, or tie it with a cord above the knee; and another minister extends his hand thus that he pushes his hands beneath the knees, then tightens a soft cord above the thigh; and another holds the cord at the head; and extend upward and downward all at once, so that the patient rises from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is good;
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If the shoulder is not in place, it requires treatment for its appearance. When the dislocation is at the front, you must first support the patient on their healthy side, then tie a cord around the root of the thigh and the area below the angle (of the affected shoulder), then tighten the cord towards the angle and the joint; then take another assistant to grasp the large part of the affected thigh, stretch it outward in the opposite direction; it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot hold it in place as we have said, you must tie the two feet of the patient together tightly with a soft cord around their two heels and knees, and let the affected leg be extended by two feet more than the others; then hang them from a post above the ground, and stretch both arms out long; then command the assistant to grasp the top of the thigh, and let another assistant hold it suspended along with the patient, as they grab hold of the thigh in the shape of a bow, because the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is at its extreme, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one with dislocated shoulder, and pulls the ligament above the affected leg properly, and also above the pelvis; then place two rods, one at the head and another at the feet; then thrust the rod between the knees of the patient so that it lines up the dislocation; and wrap moist cloths around it to prevent blistering, then each minister stretches out towards him, and the mirror places his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on a bed and press as we have said in the dislocated shoulder, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	When the dislocation is in front, it's necessary to extend the affected leg immediately, and as I have said; place the mirror on the opposite side of the dislocation, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is to the outer side, it should not extend the patient's lower body downwards, nor raise it up above the ground, but rather keep it as when a woman is dislocated to the outer side, as we have said in the lying on two beds; and let it be on its backside, and the limb extended as we have said before, and press firmly on the joint at the table; and it will be right when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then align the thighs, put the pillow, and bind them with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then unbind, put the pillow again; and if you see that they are even, bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind, and let him walk well, until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in four ways: inside and outwards, backwards, but not forwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his thigh with your hands, pull it between your hands, then bend the two sides of the thigh together; let another servant extend his foot until the thigh returns to its place, and the signs are that it should be easy for him to bend his leg at the knee slightly; put the plaster on, and bind the leg to the thigh tightly for three or four days, then release it; do not make the patient walk, until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of fractures, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes completely dislocated, from within and out of place.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs that the ankle is dislocated are when it swells and protrudes at the part where it is dislocated: the repositioning should be easy, and it must be gently extended to the hands only when it has been reduced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold the leg by the ankle, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, then lift it up, and push the foot up forcefully; do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start again because it may return; and if it cannot return in this way, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and firmly fix the stirrup (passageil) firmly in the ground between his knees, and cover with cloths so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the leg, and another person holds the healthy leg above the ankle or the knee, keeping it up at the neck of the foot; then each person should extend equally, and the stirrup should be close to the ankles of the patient to hold him down when lifting; then place the mirrors equally on the dislocation in their hands, and another person holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is in place, put the plaster and wool on top, bind firmly, and tie the thigh to the leg, keeping the nerves above the ankle from being too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding softens, tighten it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and send the patient to walk for four days; and if he goes before that term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes up, you must treat it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two [parts] are dislocated, they should be stretched gently without strain, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any direction between the thigh and the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or bed straight up, and place your foot over the affected joints, then press firmly on the foot until it returns to its original position; when it is even and there is no gap, put two small tables under the heel of the foot, then bind it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is to be restored, the patient often dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and slow; and use at first cooling remedies for the abscess, and let the patient be in God's hand if you see no hope of healing; and when you see hope, reset the limb to its place immediately as the abscess comes to life; and when the limb is in place, administer cooling remedies for the abscess, and treat the wound as necessary, with drying ointments; and if there is a break in the bone due to dislocation, and small bones are displaced, set them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, according to what I have said, for it will harm you according to your Creator, and because of the wisdom of your weapons and body.
Amen	 Amen (In English)
